Important News

Continued Report on the Riot of Japanese in Qingdao 76

Japanese Warships Arrive in Qingdao, But Soldiers Do Not Land

Japanese Protest to the Municipal Government

Report from Witness, German Doctor

Qingdao Correspondence: The case of the riot of Japanese residents in this city and the murder of Chinese people has been detailed in yesterday's news. After this case occurred, Japanese newspapers tried their best to publicize the opposite, hoping to expand the incident. Yesterday, a large meeting of Japanese residents was held in the Japanese Residents Group to discuss countermeasures. In the evening, hundreds of Japanese rioters, each secretly carrying weapons, went to Huan Tai Road and Liao Ning Road in Xiao Bao Dao to provoke trouble again. Fortunately, the Public Security Bureau dispatched security teams in advance, and all personnel were on duty patrolling and suppressing the area, paying close attention to preventing the area. All Chinese people were not allowed to pass through the area to avoid conflict, so no accident occurred. Seeing that there was no opportunity to take advantage of, the rioters dispersed late at night. After receiving an emergency telegram from the Japanese, the Japanese warship Kuma stationed in Lushun arrived in Qingdao last night. In fact, this city is as peaceful as ever and not as bad as the Japanese have publicized. Therefore, after the warship arrived in Qingdao, it docked at Pier No. 4 in Dalian, and the soldiers did not land. The municipal government has submitted a serious protest to the Japanese Consulate based on reports from all parties. However, the Japanese side not only ignored it but also sent an unreasonable protest to the municipal government. The municipal government has refuted it with reason. The details of the incident and the number of injured have been inspected by both parties together with the notary, the German famous doctor Wei Shiying. The inspection report of Wei Shiying is recorded as follows, so it is not difficult for people to distinguish the right and wrong of this matter. (1) Report from the Chinese side: This doctor examined ten injured people in the Municipal Hospital this afternoon. Three of them were slightly injured and seven were seriously injured (knife wounds). The cause of the injuries was all caused by sharp instruments (knives). Although there is no danger to life, it is not known whether pus will occur in the process. In short, this doctor observed the wounds and dared to conclude that the injured were indeed mostly injured in the back, and those who could not avoid it were also injured. (2) Report from the Japanese side: A total of sixteen injured people were inspected at the Qingdao Hospital. Most of them were skin injuries or beaten with sticks, stoned, or kicked. Three of them were injured to the bone, and it could not be determined whether the bone was injured without X-rays. Although the injured are slightly injured, there may be suppuration during the treatment period. The above report from Wei Yishi proves that the Japanese carried weapons and it was a deliberate riot, while the Chinese had no weapons and could not resist, resulting in serious injuries, and the injured People more claimed that although they were brutally victimized at that time, they still did not know why they offended the Japanese, which shows that they did not intentionally cause trouble. Also, after investigating the injured Japanese, it was found that a Korean man named Xu Daihao who sold morphine was also sent to the hospital by the Japanese to make up the numbers, which has nothing to do with this case, and it can be seen that the Japanese's intentions are cunning. (August 20th)

National Army Kills Key Red Bandit Leaders 77

Fake Army Commander Deng Yigang's Bandit Corpse Shown to the Public

Airplane Bombs Bandit Leader in Sedan Chair to Death in Ningdu

Nanchang Dispatch: The remnants of Red bandits Zhu, Mao, Peng, and Huang have recently concentrated in the Wangpi, Xiaobu, Nankeng, Liangcun, Liantang, Jiangbei Cave, Yinkeng, Zhangmushan, and Ge'ao areas bordering the four counties of Yudu, Xingguo, Yongfeng, and Ningdu, hoping to take advantage of the familiar mountainous terrain and dangerous topography to invade the National Army, attempting to succeed. Therefore, in recent days (from the beginning to mid-month), the left and right wings of the National Army, such as the Mao, Zhao, Wei, Jiang, Han, Hao, Luo, Jiang, and Cai Divisions, have braved the summer heat and fought fiercely with the Red bandits in the deep mountains and remote valleys of Xing, Yu, Yong, and Ning. The intensity of the fighting, the length of the stalemate, and the ferocity of the firepower have surpassed even the battles to recover Ningdu and Shishi. According to military sources, the main forces of Zhu and Mao, led by Peng (Dehuai), Huang (Gonglue), Lin (Biao), and others, who invaded from Ningdu on the left wing, have been defeated by Zhu Shaoliang's Third Army Group. The main forces of bandit troops led by Xiang Ying, Wu Zhonghao, Chen Yi, and Deng Gang, who invaded from Yudu and Xingguo towards the Third Route Army, have also been defeated by the right-wing army. The various armies are currently searching and suppressing the remaining bandits everywhere. Victory telegrams have been arriving in the province daily. Deng Yigang, commander of the bandit's Thirty-Fifth Army, gathered three to four thousand bandits with hundreds of guns (the rest were spears), hiding in the Datian (border area of Yudu, Ruijin, Ningdu, and Xingguo) Zhongpo area. Commander Han rushed there in the morning, first occupying the nearby mountain peaks and high grounds where the bandits were located, and then using a part of the force to charge into the bandit formation. The bandits resisted briefly and then scattered and fled over the mountains. At that time, our ambush troops fired their guns and cannons together, and bullets rained down, killing thirteen to fourteen hundred bandits and wounding over a thousand. Fake army commander Deng Yigang was also shot and killed. The wounded bandit soldiers identified Deng's body, and it was carried out for public display, which was met with great rejoicing. The scattered bandits are still being pursued by separate teams. It is reported that this operation mostly involved mountain bandits operating in the area, similar to the Miao and Yao people. The National Army inevitably faces many difficulties. Regarding reconnaissance and communication, it relies entirely on the instructions and notifications of aircraft, which is the only effective tool. It is understood that there are several squadrons, including the 1st, 3rd, and 5th, in the aviation team in Jiangxi, and most of the fighter planes are stationed in Ji'an and Fuzhou. Since Generalissimo Chiang Kai-shek appointed Mao Bangchu as the commander of the Air Force, all reconnaissance and bombing operations on the front lines are under his command. Mao also flies from the province to the front lines from time to time to inspect. For example, in the battles of Liantang and Huangpi, the aircraft were very effective. Furthermore, the headquarters recently received a report from the Aviation Department that yesterday, when an aircraft flew to the Ningdu area for reconnaissance and bombing, it saw hundreds of armed bandits escorting several large blue sedan chairs on the road from Zhukeng (Guangchang to the Fujian-Jiangxi-Ningdu main road) to Ningdu, heading east. Knowing that they were bandit leaders, they immediately dropped a heavy bomb, which exploded instantly. The sedan chairs were shattered into powder, and the armed bandits scattered and fled. The bandit leaders in the sedan chairs must have been killed, and so on. According to front-line reports, the bandits in Huangpi and Xiaopu are from the two major groups of Zhu and Mao. Recently, under the intense firepower pressure from the left-wing army, they fled east along Zhukeng, passing through Kuzhu and Qianshan north of Guangchang, towards the Fujian border. This confirms the above news that those traveling east towards Zhukeng in sedan chairs must be Zhu, Mao, and other leaders. (August 17th)

Zhu Qinglan's Disaster Narrative 78

Dogs gnaw on white bones, sinews still remain... This is the scene in Shaanxi and Gansu.

Birds peck at fresh corpses, blood not yet dry... This is the battlefield along the Ping-Han Railway.

Disaster relief: First save the people, then discuss relief efforts.

Tianjin Dispatch: Mr. Zhu Ziqiao, in response to the telegram invitation from Song Ziwen and others from the Flood Relief Emergency Committee, arrived in Tianjin last night (the 18th) and will take the Pingpu express train south at 10 p.m. tonight. The reporter interviewed him at the Qunxian Hotel and had a long conversation, inquiring about the situation in Shaanxi and Gansu and his opinions on going south to handle flood relief. According to his remarks, as follows:

This time, I entered Gansu from Shaanxi, only reaching Liangzhou (Wuwei County), when I received a telegram from Shanghai urging me to return. However, the situation in Shaanxi and Gansu is gradually improving. When I went to Shaanxi and Gansu the year before last, in all the counties I visited, the ground was without grass, the trees were without bark (having been scraped off and eaten by the disaster victims), and the houses were like empty shells. No chickens or dogs could be

Page 14

heard. This time, returning to the old places, although the houses are still like empty shells, the trees already have bark, the ground already grows grass, and the sounds of chickens and dogs can be heard. As for grains, the low-lying, water-adjacent fields have all been planted and have a five- or six-tenths chance of harvest. The highland areas without water are still barren mountains. Our China is truly unfortunate. Disasters of floods, droughts, hail, bandits, and soldiers come one after another. Disaster relief is only a temporary emergency measure. What should be done after disaster relief? Most disaster relief organizers have not considered this. They only seek to treat the symptoms, not the root cause. Given the size of China, there will inevitably be disasters every year, and disaster relief will be needed every year. Thus, disaster relief organizers will become a permanent enterprise. The disaster in Gansu, which resulted in hundreds of thousands of deaths, was caused by inconvenient transportation and the failure to develop water conservancy. The canals built during the Tang Dynasty can still be faintly discerned today. The ancients built the country on agriculture, so they paid attention to water conservancy. If modern rulers had continued the policies of the ancients and engaged in water conservancy construction, widely opening canals on the Guan River in the provinces of Gansu, Shaanxi, Suiyuan, and Shanxi to divert the floodwaters of the Yellow River, then how could the provinces in the Yellow River basin suffer from floods every year? Furthermore, extending this, if all the provinces in the Huai River and Yangtze River basins could strive for water conservancy construction, then why would China's agricultural products lag behind the world? The China International Famine Relief Commission is doing very well in Shaanxi and Gansu. The first step is to develop transportation, and the second step is to develop water conservancy. Currently, the Binwei motor road (i.e., from Bin County on the Shaanxi border to Wuwei County in Gansu, over 1,000 li long) is under construction. This is a method of providing work in exchange for relief. The entire road can be completed next year. The Commission has hired many engineers to survey other routes. I preside over the Shaanxi-Gansu Emergency Relief Committee. After completing the spring relief, the remaining funds were used to distribute seeds. I originally wanted to organize rural cooperatives, but because there were villages without people, or people without land, it was impossible to do so. Therefore, I investigated farmers who had land but no ability to cultivate it, and provided loans appropriately to enable them to purchase cattle, horses, and farm implements, to be repaid with an interest rate of one and a half percent after the autumn harvest, as a form of restriction. As for the conflicts between Hui and Han in Gansu, I believe it is a political problem, not a national problem. Those who hold military power occupy their respective areas and do not yield to each other. The newly appointed Chairman of Gansu Province, Ma Hongbin, can only exercise his authority in one corner and cannot extend it to the entire province. The conflicts between Hui and Han have a long history. Rulers have always used high-pressure tactics to quickly quell disputes, but they do not know that the greater the pressure, the greater the reaction. Therefore, grievances are repaid with grievances, endlessly. I hope that the rulers will find ways to instruct the people that the dead are already gone and cannot be brought back to life. The only thing to do is to comfort the surviving families, transform them with virtue, and promote the spirit of Hui-Han friendship. Over time, they will naturally be able to live in peace. Lixian County is where the Hui-Han killings were the most tragic. Only nine people with white hair were left in the entire county. We do not need to witness the tragedy; hearing about it is enough to bring tears to our eyes. On my way back north, I received a telegram from the Battlefield Emergency Relief Committee inviting me to assist in everything. So I got off the train in Baoding and boarded the train from Zhengzhou. Passing through Shunde, I could see new graves stacked up all the way to Baoding, with Wangdu being the most tragic. The battlefield burial teams all did their work perfunctorily. Those who died in the trenches were buried in the trenches, covered with soil. Those who died on the plains were mostly buried in mass graves, but the burial pits were too shallow, and many were dug out by wild dogs. One often sees several dogs or a flock of birds fighting over a corpse, covered in blood, too horrible to bear. In this hot weather, corpses buried too shallowly are evaporated by the sun and easily transmit epidemics through the spread of air. I mentioned above that in Gansu, I could already hear the crowing of chickens and the barking of dogs, which I considered a sign that the situation was gradually improving. However, occasionally walking through ancient temples and deserted suburbs, one still occasionally finds the tragic scene of dogs gnawing on white bones. Now I see the tragic scene of new battlefields. An ancient poem says, "Dogs gnaw on white bones, sinews still remain; birds peck at fresh corpses, blood not yet dry." This can be used as a portrayal of today's disasters. I suggested to the Battlefield Emergency Relief Committee: (1) Reorganize burial teams to set out and rebury the corpses, digging pits more than four feet deep. (2) Investigate the houses destroyed by the people and provide appropriate compensation so that they have homes to return to, to avoid becoming displaced. Currently, the Committee has transported four trainloads of relief grain and a considerable amount of relief funds and is providing relief. As for how to deal with the floods in the south, I am not yet clear. I believe that disaster relief must first save people. More small steamships should be hired to quickly transport the disaster victims to Xujiapeng on the Wu-Chang Railway, where the terrain is higher, and more mat sheds should be erected to shelter them from the wind and rain. Then, funds should be raised to transport grain to provide emergency relief. Mr. Zhang Jian once said that the Huai River diversion project is crucial and cannot be delayed any longer; otherwise, in thirty to fifty years, Wuhan will inevitably be flooded. However, it has been delayed for ten years, and the Huai River has not been diverted. Mr. Zhang's prediction has been confirmed today, which is regrettable. Lou Xiangqing, a member of the Shaanxi-Gansu Emergency Relief Committee, hosted a banquet for Mr. Zhu at the Huizhong Hotel at 7 p.m. tonight, reporting on his inspection of the disaster situation in Shaanxi and Gansu and inviting representatives from various charitable organizations to attend. The guests and hosts did not disperse until 9 p.m., and Zhu immediately boarded the train south. (August 19th)

Yellow River Water Levels Drop in Shandong Province 79

Situation Near Luokou Somewhat Stable, Downstream Works Still Need Strong Protection

Jinan Dispatch: Regarding the Yellow River situation, as of last night (the 20th), a telegram from Shanzhou reported a stable water level, the same as the 17th. In the upper reaches of this province, Lishangtun water level dropped four inches, Sunlou water level dropped one foot three inches. In the middle reaches, Guanzhuang in Dong'a County dropped eight inches, Qihe water level dropped three inches, and Luokou water level dropped two inches. The situation seems to have stabilized somewhat. According to river bureau officials, a stable water level in Shanzhou and a dropping water level in this province means that even if Shanzhou rises again in the future, this province will be able to accommodate it after the subsidence. According to this view, if there is no major rise again, there may be no danger this year. River Affairs Bureau Director Zhang Lianjia returned to Luokou from the downstream last night and went to Beidianzi in the upstream this morning to cross the river and inspect the upstream. The Qingcheng County Magistrate was reprimanded by the River Affairs Bureau in a telegram for his ineffective rescue efforts and disregard for work defense. The telegram read: "To Changfuzhen and the chief magistrate of Qingcheng (named Shi Zi) and the director of the Public Security Bureau: Since the beginning of autumn, the river water has been rising sharply, and the various sections of the project are in danger. The chairman and the civil affairs department have repeatedly telegraphed the county magistrate and the director of the Public Security Bureau to quickly go to work, gather laborers to assist in prevention, and the bureau has also telegraphed to comply with the cases. However, it was found that the county magistrate and the director of the Public Security Bureau delayed until the bureau chief personally came to the worksite before the county magistrate arrived. After the county magistrate left, the laborers scattered, disregarded the merit order, and acted perfunctorily, which is extremely inappropriate. The autumn floods are long, and the water source is abundant. If there is any negligence, the relationship will be far-reaching. Therefore, we order the director of the County Public Security Bureau to comply with the merit order, immediately go to work, and quickly assemble laborers to the various dangerous sections on the north and south banks that have been transferred, station them permanently to work, and assist the section defense officers in strictly guarding to ensure safety, and report the handling situation at any time. Sincerely. Director Zhang Lianjia (seal)"

River Affairs Bureau Director Zhang Lianjia went to the downstream yesterday to inspect the river works and arrived at Damajia in the Tianjin border on the north bank that night. Because a dangerous section suddenly appeared there last night, Zhang immediately supervised the rescue work there. Today, the situation has stabilized somewhat. Zhang telegraphed the provincial government from Damajia, urgently requesting the provincial government to continue ordering the county magistrates and public security bureau directors of the counties along the river to go to the embankment to supervise the flood rescue work. Also, Beidianzi, 30 li northwest of Luokou on the south bank of Changqing, which was in danger the night before last, is now stable. This afternoon, the Luokou water mark dropped another two inches, still nine zhang two chi seven inches above sea level, and the situation is slightly more stable than yesterday. Licheng County Magistrate Zhou Zongyao gathered more than a thousand laborers in Mengjiaquan to supervise the flood rescue work. The following is the text of Zhang Lianjia's telegram to the provincial government: "Urgent to Chairman Han Jun of the Jinan Provincial Government: The director is currently at Damajia in Lijin. All the works along the way are tight, especially the downstream. At Daoxu Wangwangzhuang in Putai County, the water level is only three feet above the lowest point of the levee. At Xiaolizhuang in Lijin, the water level is about two feet above the levee. Eight or nine out of ten of the dams are overflowing, with the water depth on the dams varying from two to three feet. All are running Zibo. Fortunately, before the great flood, the foundations of the dams were still solid and well-maintained, and they were not lost. We have ordered each section to cut willows, bundle soil, or add pressed sacks for temporary relief. There is no major danger at present, but the downstream river water has not subsided. If protection is slightly lax, danger will be inevitable. We still urgently request that you telegraphed the county magistrates and public security bureau directors of the counties along the river to be permanently stationed at work, supervise the laborers to go to the embankment to check the water, and assist the defense soldiers in fighting hard to protect it, so as to avoid negligence. River Affairs Bureau Director Zhang Lianjia (seal not affixed) (August 21st)"

Han Fuju Will Go to Peiping 80

Will Visit Zhang Xueliang and Then Go to Bianliang to Meet Liu Zhi

Jinan Dispatch: Liu Zhi's representative, Li Guosheng, arrived in Jinan and went to the provincial government at 2 p.m. yesterday to visit Han Fuju and discuss everything. Han left Li at the provincial government and hosted a banquet to welcome him, with all the important figures in attendance. This morning, the reporter visited Li and learned that the results of yesterday's meeting with Director Han were extremely satisfactory. (1) Regarding the Shi Hanzhang issue, Han said that he and Hanzhang had been through thick and thin for twenty years and had a deep friendship. He was surrounded by reactionaries, and I had repeatedly and earnestly advised him, and many others had also advised him, but he was ultimately stubborn. For the sake of maintaining the overall situation, the central government and Chairman Liu had no choice but to stop him. I cannot harm the public for personal reasons, so I obey the commander-in-chief's orders. This is his own fault, and there is nothing that can be done. (2) Regarding the issue of Director Han going to Henan, Han said that Henan was a place of old friendships. Chairman Liu and I had shared weal and woe and had long wanted to go to reminisce. Recently, I was appointed by the central government as the Director of Qingxiang (cleanup) in Shandong and Henan. Regarding the various issues of Qingxiang and bandit suppression in the two provinces, I need to discuss them with Chairman Liu in person and ask for his help. However, due to busy official duties, I have not been able to go. Now that the reorganization of Shi's troops is underway, I cannot get away. Once the reorganization of Shi's troops is completed in the next few days, I will prepare to set off. As for the issue of jointly attacking Liu Guitang's troops, Director Han ordered the commander of the 29th Division, Cao Fulin, to set off with his troops yesterday. Liu's remaining troops can be resolved within a few days. I will stay for a few days and then return to Henan to report. According to reliable sources in the provincial government, Deputy Commander Zhang Xueliang had previously invited Han to Peiping for a meeting. Han had not been able to go because of the reorganization of Shi's troops. Now that the reorganization of Shi's troops is complete, he plans to first go to Peiping to visit Zhang in the next few days, and then take the Ping-Han Railway to Bianliang to meet Liu Zhi and discuss all Qingxiang matters in Shandong and Henan. After returning, he will immediately begin a major Qingxiang operation. (August 21st)

Jinan Court Investigates the Zhu Shude Case 81

Chairman Han's Wife Questioned and Found the Gun

Jinan Dispatch: The provincial Second Experimental Elementary School shooting death case, after Chairman Han Fuju summoned [the parties] for questioning and discovered the source of the handgun, has been referred to the local court for investigation in preparation for prosecution. The court has sent two official letters to the Third Public Security Sub-bureau outside the city. The first letter asked whether the nearby police officers on duty had heard gunshots at the time of the incident at 5 p.m. on July 27th. Because the positions of the sub-bureau's guards were far from Shenjia Alley, the police officers on duty at that time did not hear any gunshots. The second letter asked when Officer Yang went to Wang Weijun's house to check the household registration on the day of the incident and when he received a phone call to go and see what had happened. It also asked where the bullet casing was found and turned over to the court for reference. Officer Yang Yichao of the First Sub-bureau was ordered to submit a detailed report yesterday. According to Officer Yang's report, at 6 p.m. on the 27th of last month, he and census police officer Wang Benzheng made a random check of Wang Weijun's house in Shenjia Alley and there was no activity. At around 7 p.m., he received a phone call from the general affairs section of the main bureau and returned with the police to knock on the door. He asked Weijun's wife, Liu Hesheng, who initially did not admit that a murder had occurred. Later, Wang Weijun and Dr. He Delin of Huamei Hospital arrived at Wang's residence and went to the west room of the hospital. The rickshaw puller Zhang Jigui lit a lamp and He Delin said that she could no longer be saved. At around 9 p.m., the court sent personnel to examine the body, etc. Ms. Zhu died in bed, and the gun was thrown under the bed. The abandoned bullet casing was picked up from the ground by the local guard Wang Yuan inside the door between the south room and the west room of Wang Weijun's house while sweeping the floor on the afternoon of the 28th. Yesterday, a detailed report was submitted, and the bullet casing was also delivered to the local court. Today (the 20th) at 9 a.m., the local court also sent Wang Weijun's rickshaw puller, Zhang Jigui, to the court. Prosecutor Liu Rongshan was present in the Third Investigation Room to question him about Wang Weijun and Zhu Shude forming a family in Xiaowangfu in August and September of last year. Zhang answered in detail about Ms. Zhu Shuxin continuing her studies. Li Shijun's daughter-in-law in Tianjin wrote a letter expressing sympathy for her situation and offering to help with her future tuition. Ms. Zhu has already replied to the letter, expressing her deep gratitude for her kindness. She politely declined the offer of financial assistance. It is also heard that Chairman Han's wife, Ji Ganqing, was extremely saddened by the tragic death of Zhu Shude and went to great lengths to ask Wang Weijun's maid, Chen Wangshi, and finally found the source of the handgun. Seeing that her younger sister, Shuxin, was eager to study but lacked the funds for her studies, she expressed sympathy. It is heard that she also told Zhu that she was willing to fund Zhu Shuxin's studies in Nanjing.

Shuanghesheng Leather Factory in Harbin Burned Down 82

The only domestic industry was burned down due to electrical fire, with losses of more than 5 million yuan.

Harbin Dispatch: The Shuanghesheng Leather Factory, the only industry of its kind in the country, and the Yuqingde Woolen Mill in Harbin are both the most promising enterprises run by Chinese. The owner of the factory is Zhang Tingge. Zhang is from Yexian County, Shandong Province, and is currently the chairman of the Harbin Chamber of Commerce and the chairman of the Municipal Self-Government Association. The Shuanghesheng Brewery in Peiping and the Shuanghesheng Flour Mill in Harbin were both founded independently by Zhang, starting in the 7th year of the Republic of China, and have been in operation for 12 years. Initially, the German technicians hired were not successful in their research, and the products made were not suitable, resulting in huge losses. It almost went bankrupt in the middle. Zhang persevered and invested over 7 million yuan in national currency. It was only in the last five years that it began to make a profit. The leather produced, such as that supplied to leather boot shops in and outside the city for purchase, was very popular and was comparable to foreign goods. This year, due to the depression in the gold industry, and with enough stock for a year's sales, it stopped work a month ago. Recently, because 1,000 raw sheepskins were purchased and needed to be made quickly to avoid spoilage, work was started on the 17th. At 10:20 a.m. that morning, while the workers were working, they suddenly saw fire on the roof of the south building of the factory. The entire workforce stopped working and took out the factory's own water dragon to put out the fire. However, the fire was caused by an electrical short circuit, starting between the iron cover of the ceiling and spreading very quickly, making it difficult to extinguish. At the same time, well water could not be used, so water troughs were used to fetch water for extinguishing. At that time, the scorching sun was in the sky, and a southwest wind suddenly rose, increasing the fire. In less than half an hour, it had spread beyond control. The factory urgently telegraphed the city fire department to come quickly for rescue. The Daoli fire engines rushed over. Because the factory was far outside the city in Quanhe, more than ten miles from the city, and the roads were muddy, the fire engines could not advance after reaching 20th Street outside the city. Some firefighters had no choice but to wade barefoot, carrying grappling hooks. Although they arrived at the fire scene, they could not climb up because the fire was on the roof of the building and the fire ladder had not been brought. They could only protect everything around the burning area. The Jiangfang Navy Barracks were located behind the factory. When the sailors saw that the fire was already large, they borrowed a water dragon from the Jiangbei shipyards and helped to extinguish it. Because they were located downwind, and the water dragon was small, the extinguishing was ineffective. The sailors were smoked by the smoke and fire and found it difficult to stand, so they returned to the barracks to protect their own homes. By about 2 p.m., all 500 rooms of the factory's buildings had been burned down. The sound of explosions from the machinery, gasoline, and wooden frames stored in the factory continued. The two accounting rooms in the northeast corner of the factory had also been engulfed, and the warehouse where goods were stored and the flat rooms where machinery was stored were also in danger of being burned. The fire engines of the fire department, blocked several miles away, were helpless. The factory manager, He Guochen, came up with a plan. He borrowed a large ship from the Northeast Shipping Bureau and told the fire engines to board the ship from 12th Street, bypass the factory from Quanhe, and connect the various fire engine water dragons to draw water from the river for extinguishing. The fire department followed the plan and arrived at the fire site at 3:30 p.m. Because the shore was muddy, the fire engines still could not get ashore. They connected the water dragons and drew water from the river to pour on the flames. By this time, not a single factory building was intact. Only the warehouses and accounting rooms were sprayed with water, which fortunately protected them. The fire was not extinguished until about 5 p.m. The fire department returned to the city after it was extinguished. It is estimated that 500 rooms in the north and south buildings of the factory, one accounting office, 17 tanning machines, 40 soaking machines, 4 planing machines, 2 cutting machines, 2 softening machines, 2 polishing machines, 1 stretching machine, 3 engines, and 3 large and small boilers were burned down, totaling losses of more than 5 million yuan in national currency. The insurance amount, with three companies, was only 1 million Haikwan taels, with actual losses of more than 4 million. Fortunately, the warehouse was not burned, and the machinery storage room was not burned, and there were still dozens of pieces of goods and machinery worth over a million yuan. However, at a time when the market is depressed and finances are extremely stagnant, the factory has suffered such a huge loss and has no ability to recover. (August 17th)

Important News Two

Records of the Second Jiangsu Provincial Congress 83

Closing Ceremony Held on the Afternoon of the Twenty-Second

Zhenjiang Dispatch: The Second Jiangsu Provincial Congress held its eighth meeting at 9:00 AM on the twenty-second at Boxian Park in Zhenjiang. Seventy-five delegates were present. The presidium elected Ge Jianshi as chairman. After the leadership led in paying respects, the discussion of proposals continued: (1) A proposal to devise methods for rescuing the province from its extraordinarily severe flooding. (Resolution) Passed. The methods were divided into two categories: immediate and fundamental. (A) Immediate Measures: 1. The provincial government's budget for the 20th year of the Republic includes a total of 400,000 yuan for disaster relief. The Finance Department should allocate this amount promptly for emergency relief efforts. 2. Telegraph the Central Relief Committee to allocate one million yuan for emergency relief in the disaster-stricken areas of Jiangnan and Jiangbei in this province. 3. The provincial government should promptly purchase one million yuan worth of food, with 500,000 yuan for rice and 500,000 yuan for wheat flour, to relieve the disaster victims in various counties. 4. Petition the Central Government to allow all national salvation funds in the counties to be used for disaster relief in those counties. 5. Allocate and borrow unspent funds from the provincial government and construction funds and special water conservancy funds retained by various counties. 6. Party and government agencies and organizations in the disaster-stricken counties should establish disaster relief committees to investigate the total food production in each county and handle all relief matters. 7. No grain from any county in this province may be transported out of the county without the order of the local government or the consent of the county's disaster relief committee. Speculation and hoarding by unscrupulous merchants are strictly prohibited. 8. County warehouses should actively store grain and rigorously clear out old, empty grain reserves. 9. No additional acreage tax should be levied this year. In disaster-stricken areas, county governments should conduct detailed investigations and reduce or exempt land taxes and rents accordingly. 10. Request the provincial government to issue public bonds as appropriate for relief and work relief. (B) Fundamental Measures: 1. The central and provincial governments should immediately follow the late Premier's teachings and implement the Huai River diversion project. This project must be completed within two years. The Huai River diversion should be based on the principle of simultaneously directing it to the sea and the Yangtze River. 2. The Grand Canal should be dredged immediately, and unemployed people near the drainage tributaries should be hired to excavate them. 3. Allocate unused construction bonds as special funds for water conservancy, adopt work-for-relief methods, and expedite the dredging of waterways, riverbeds, and rivers entering the sea, the Yangtze River, and lakes north and south of the Yangtze River. The Construction Department must announce the entire plan within one month and implement it immediately. 4. The Provincial Department of Agriculture and Mining should focus on afforestation this year, soliciting donations from local people in various counties or using local public funds for afforestation. Appoint personnel to guide and supervise the implementation of this plan. (2) A proposal to reform the politics of this province. (Resolution) The review report and the supplementary opinions of the delegates will be compiled and submitted to the Resolution Drafting Committee for collation. (3) A proposal to petition the Central Government to swiftly arrest and bring to justice Tan Shuqing, who arbitrarily killed Party members, to avenge the Party and provide generous compensation to the families of the victims, Comrades Chen and Zhang. (Resolution) A. Petition the Central Government to swiftly remove Tan Shuqing from his post, bring him to justice, and punish him to the fullest extent of the law. B. Petition the Central Government to provide generous compensation to the families of the deceased Comrades Chen Siheng and Zhang Jingchu. (4) A proposal to request the provincial government to strictly prevent Zhang Cha, a major local tyrant in Jiangsu, who has been on the run for three years, from engaging in extensive activities in an attempt to escape punishment. (Resolution) 1. The General Assembly Secretariat should immediately notify the provincial government that his property should not be returned before the local tyrant case is adjudicated, and report the case to the Commander-in-Chief's Office for review. 2. The Provincial Executive Committee should notify the High Court to promptly summon the case for trial and judgment. 3. The Provincial Executive Committee should petition the Central Government not to be confused. By this point in the meeting, only sixty-eight delegates were present. (There were actually one hundred and forty-nine delegates to the congress.) This was less than the legal quorum, so the chairman declared the meeting adjourned.

At 2:00 PM, the ninth meeting was convened. Seventy-eight delegates were present. Huang Yuren chaired the meeting. After the leadership led in paying respects, the following urgent proposals were discussed: (1) A proposal to request the Central Government to immediately remove and punish Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting, who has shown no results since taking office and has often engaged in acts of national humiliation and loss of sovereignty, in order to purify the officialdom and maintain national discipline. (Resolution) Passed. (2) A proposal to investigate Chen Hexian, a member of the Provincial Government and concurrently the Director of the Department of Education, who is ignorant of education, has achieved nothing in his two years in office, has colluded with academic cliques, has used elements of the National State Doctrine faction, has disregarded Party principles, and has undermined local education, which is a violation of Party discipline. Should this assembly petition the Central Government to instruct the National Government to swiftly remove him from office and punish him as a warning to others? Please decide by public vote. (Resolution) Passed. (3) A proposal to investigate Wang Boling, a member of the Provincial Government, who has been drawing a salary every month since taking office but has never come to the province to work. The Provincial Party Consolidation Committee has previously sent letters urging him to attend Provincial Government meetings, but he has ignored them. This is dereliction of duty. Should this assembly petition the Central Government to instruct the National Government to swiftly remove him from office and punish him in order to uphold the law and discipline? (Resolution) Passed. (4) A proposal to set a five-month deadline for the suppression of bandits. (Proposed by the delegate from Shuyang County.) (5) A proposal that the General Assembly notify the provincial government to order the county magistrates to suppress bandit gangs within a specified period. (6) A proposal that bandits are rampant in Suqian, Suining, and other counties, and the people are living in misery. They should be suppressed as soon as possible in order to secure the good people and pacify the local area. (Proposed by the delegate from Suqian County.) The above three proposals were discussed together. (Resolution) Send a letter to the provincial government to consult with the Pacification Superintendent's Office and set a three-month deadline for the suppression of bandits. (7) A proposal that the construction projects in Jiangbei, in this province, should prioritize river management first. (Resolution) Passed. (8) A proposal to strictly prohibit land and acreage taxes from exceeding one percent of the land value in order to alleviate the suffering of the people of Jiangsu. (Resolution) Passed. (9) A proposal that the General Assembly Declaration, which has been drafted by the Drafting Committee, be reviewed and passed. (Resolution) Amended and passed. (10) A proposal that all cases not yet discussed be referred to the Executive Committee for review and handling. (Resolution) Passed.

General Idea of the Declaration: The Declaration of the Third Provincial Congress states the responsibility of the Party during the period of political tutelage based on the resolutions of the Congress, actively completing the work of self-government as a model for the provinces. The most important tasks at present are (1) promoting Party affairs in this province, (2) reforming the politics of this province, and (3) providing relief for the floods in this province. The entire text will be revised by Ge Jianshi and Ma Yinbing.

Closing Ceremony: After the discussion of the proposals was completed, the closing ceremony was held. The ceremony was conducted as usual. Huang Yuren delivered the closing address, stating that this Congress had been successfully completed and would be sufficient to promote Party affairs and politics in this province in the future. He hoped that the delegates from various counties would return to their villages and conduct widespread propaganda among the people so that all the resolutions could be realized. Finally, slogans were shouted, and the meeting was adjourned.

Post-Disaster Agricultural Relief in Jiangsu Province 84

Expanding the Cattle Protection Movement and Promoting Famine Relief Crops

Zhenjiang Dispatch: The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Agriculture believes that the floods in Jiangsu Province this year have been extraordinarily severe. Not only have many fields been flooded, but the displacement of farmers and the loss and drowning of cattle have also been countless. Currently, people and cattle are living together on the banks of the Grand Canal and in relatively high places. People have no food, and cattle lack fodder. Farmers are too busy taking care of themselves to care for the cattle, so they are willing to sell them at a low price to prolong their lives for a few more days. Unscrupulous merchants and cattle dealers are further suppressing the price. If this continues, they will all be sold to slaughterhouses. What will be done for spring plowing next year? Protecting cattle is an urgent priority. Furthermore, due to the heavy losses from the autumn harvest in various counties, except for the areas below the river, where it is inconvenient to replant suitable crops due to the water not receding, the weather in the other disaster-stricken counties has cleared up, and the water has gradually receded. It is essential to guide farmers to replant autumn crops, such as buckwheat, turnips, and beans. Providing loans for seeds is also an urgent matter. The department has now formulated separate measures to help various counties recover from the agricultural disaster. Details are described below: (A) Expanding the Cattle Protection Movement: (1) Allocate 10,000 yuan from the emergency flood relief funds this year, and continue to allocate 50,000 to 60,000 yuan from the second relief funds to purchase fodder. At the same time, order the autumn harvest counties in Jiangnan to raise funds and transport them to the disaster areas to be loaned at low prices or distributed free of charge. (2) Order county governments to encourage farmers to preserve cattle and prohibit cattle from leaving the county. Provincial and county governments should organize cattle protection committees. Disaster-stricken counties should also establish one cattle foster home, all of which should be organized by local community organizations and managed and fed by the county agricultural improvement field. (B) Promoting Famine Relief Crops: The department will purchase famine relief crop seeds worth 20,000 to 50,000 yuan and distribute them to farmers according to the circumstances of each county. The above two measures have been submitted to the Provincial Government Committee yesterday (the twenty-first) and have been resolved and passed. If the funds arrive on time, they can be implemented immediately. (Twenty-second)

Local Dispatches

Songjiang 85

County Magistrate and Education Director Go to the Provincial Capital on Duty: County Magistrate Shen and Education Director Ni were summoned to the provincial capital by telegram from the Director of the Department of Civil Affairs yesterday to discuss important public matters. It is said to be related to the proposed reduction of education funding in the county. Therefore, the joint conference of teachers and staff of primary and secondary schools here has stated that if the goal of restoring the funding is not achieved, the start of the school year will be postponed.

Investigating the Caojing Robbery Case: In Caojing, Punan, on the tenth map, Chen Jin's family was broken into by more than a dozen robbers armed with rifles and pistols the other night. They searched and robbed at will, taking clothes, ornaments, and other items, causing considerable losses and injuring Chen Jin's grandmother, Chen Shenshi. The victim reported the case to the Public Security Bureau, which forwarded it to the county government, requesting the county court to send personnel to the countryside to investigate. It also ordered the land and water police teams to strictly arrest the perpetrators and bring them to justice.

Qingpu 86

Bandits Arrested in Shitang Village: Four patrol boats from the Jinshang Xishui Public Security Team in the fourth district of the county arrived at Shitang Village the other night. They fired several shots to intimidate the village and then searched it in different directions. As a result, they arrested four people, including the bandit Da Mulin, and took them back to the Jinze Corps headquarters for transfer to the county government for review.

Workers Arrested in Wujia Kiln: The other day, eight plainclothes police officers from the thirteenth district of the county and the seventh district of Songjiang, near Tangqiao Town, were led into Wujia Kiln by a woman. She pointed out four workers from Jinshanwei. As the police were about to arrest them, the four men jumped out of the window to escape. The police fired shots and chased after them, capturing three and allowing one to escape. That night, they were escorted to the Songjiang Bandit Suppression Headquarters for review.

Suzhou 87

The Jiangsu Education Tide Near the Start of the School Year: Educational circles in Wu County are dissatisfied with the Bureau of Education's austerity policies and have expressed their opposition. They have repeatedly petitioned the bureau, the county, and the Department of Education without effect. The principals of the schools have now decided that the minimum standard must be the budget for the nineteenth year of the Republic. Yesterday (the twenty-second), 171 principals jointly submitted a petition to the Department of Education, requesting that it send personnel to Suzhou to investigate as the start of the school year is approaching.

Zhao Weixian Escorted to Shanghai: Zhao Weixian, who lives at No. 3 Fuxing Bridge Lane, is the ninth son-in-law of the Shanghai gentleman Zhu Baoshan. He is currently the battalion commander of the Fourth Battalion of the Bengbu Tax Police. He was arrested on the twenty-first as a suspect in the Wei Tingrong kidnapping case. Yesterday (the twenty-second), personnel from the Shanghai Court came to Suzhou to escort him to Shanghai. Commander Wang of the Tax Police Independent Regiment telegraphed the Public Security Bureau, requesting that Zhao be released on bail because he is a current police officer. The Public Security Bureau immediately telegraphed back to the commander that he had been escorted to Shanghai.

Public Security Team Intercepts Bandit Boat and Rescues Abductee: On the nineteenth, the third team of the fourteenth team of the Wujiang Water Public Security encountered three bandit boats in Taihu Lake near Miaoqian. The two sides exchanged fire fiercely. As a result, two boats escaped, and one was intercepted. A hostage, Song Gaosheng, was rescued. He was escorted to the Third District Office of Suzhou on the afternoon of the twenty-second. According to his account, he is twelve years old, from Songjiazhuang, Hengta. His father's name is Yaokun. He was kidnapped by bandits along with Song Shunjin and Song Wuguan on August 7. The two, Wuguan, etc. are still on the bandit boat.

Changshu 88

The District Office and the Construction Bureau Contend for Rickshaw Donations: In the past, the first district office of this county released 240 rickshaws. All donations were collected by the district office. In November of last year, the Construction Bureau considered it necessary to add more rickshaws to Changshu, so it added 60 rickshaws, which were donated by the Construction Bureau. Since then, the boundaries have been clearly defined. Previously, the Construction Bureau believed that the rickshaw business was a business that should be handled by the Construction Bureau, and the monthly donations should not go to the district office. Therefore, it listed the reasons and, according to the regulations, presented them to the county government, requesting the first district office to hand over the donations. The county government ordered Wu Xinheng, the district chief of the first district office, to reply himself. Soon, District Chief Wu also listed the reasons and presented them to the county government according to the provincial regulations, expressing his unwillingness to hand over the donations. Now, the Construction Bureau will directly ask the Provincial Construction Department to review and seize the donations.

The Party Committee's Accusation Case is Transferred to Suzhou for Trial: With respect to the allegation by Tong Shizhong, a Party member from Meili, that Shi Minyong, a supervisory committee member of the county Party headquarters, defrauded him of money, although County Magistrate Tan of this county had accepted the case, the Party Supervisory Committee has the power to audit the government at the same level. It applied to the High Court for permission to transfer jurisdiction. Lin Wan, the president of the High Court, handed it over to Li Mian, the chief of the Second Criminal Division, for a decision. He considered it reasonable. The decision has now arrived at the county. All kinds of documents and files in this case have been presented to Suzhou and transferred to the Wu County District Court by the High Court for trial.

Yixing 89

An Eighty-Eight-Year-Old Man Gets Married: Deng Bingnan (also known as Lao San) from Hubei, who has been living at the foot of Yangling Mountain in Dongda Temple, Zhangzhu Town, for more than sixty years, is now eighty-eight years old. He has reclaimed more than a hundred acres of barren land and has some savings. His late wife has been dead for more than thirty years. He adopted his nephew as his son. His nephew's wife was kidnapped by bandits a few years ago but was later ransomed and returned home. He treats both of his nephew's wives as if they were his own daughters and is quite content. A few days ago, he was persuaded by a fellow villager to marry a fifty-two-year-old widow as his second wife. He was formally married the other day. The two elderly newlyweds also rode in sedan chairs at the time of the wedding. After the marriage, they were very fond of each other. People nearby were all talking about it as a beautiful story. The whole of Yixing's Xushe Becomes a Waterland: Since the beginning of summer, the continuous rain has lasted for more than ten days. The severity of the flood is the greatest it has been in thirty years. In addition, Xushe is located downstream of Liyang and has low-lying terrain. The accumulated water upstream flowed down, causing most of the houses to be flooded, and countless livestock drowned. It was a sea of water, a heartbreaking sight. The water in the city was several feet deep, and shops were completely closed, and traffic was cut off. The river water is still rising, and the wind is raging, causing the dikes to collapse one after another. In places like Waimuwei, Etouwei, and Dingtongwei, about tens of thousands of acres of farmland were flooded. The disaster victims were in danger of starvation, and the city residents were sighing about the fish. It was a real catastrophe. Countless disaster victims are now lying in the flood, crying for food. They are eagerly awaiting relief.

Wuxi 90

Disputes over Unsuccessful Appeals: Since its establishment, the Wuxi County Court has acted in accordance with the law in all its measures. However, even with the most careful planning, negligence is inevitable. For example, Xu Quanlao, a gambling offender who had already served his sentence and been released, was mistakenly arrested again as a soil smuggling offender and escorted to Suzhou. Only after questioning by the High Court did it become clear that he was another person. Despite repeated arguments, he was still not released. He has now filed a petition. Recently, Han Zhian from Suqian was falsely accused by Wang Laoer of interfering with his family last winter. The county government transferred the case to the court, which sentenced Han Zhian to one year of imprisonment for enticing on June 19 of this year. On June 27, the defendant Han Zhian officially received the judgment. Dissatisfied with the judgment, he immediately drafted a petition and sent it to the County Court and the High Court, as well as a petition for dissatisfaction. He formally delivered them on July 6, within the appeal period, with a receipt. However, he did not receive any approval. The other day, Yang Keqian, the concurrent prosecutor, suddenly summoned the appellant Han Zhian to the court, saying that the appeal period had long expired and he must now be sent to prison. Han asked why, and the prosecutor Yang checked the files again, saying that there was only an appeal to the High Court, but no petition. Han insisted that he could use the receipt as proof, but Yang still did not believe him and ordered him to be returned to custody. Han, who had been unjustly implicated, has already filed an appeal and requested compensation for damages.

Spontaneous Combustion of a Stove Leads to a Tragic Incident: The owner of Shengxinchang Shoe Store on Guanqian Street in the city, Lu Gerong, who is related to him, is thirty-seven years old. He recently came to Wuxi for medical treatment due to illness. He has now recovered slightly. The other night, he was cooking food with a foreign stove when he suddenly fainted, causing the stove to ignite his limbs and chest. He was seriously injured and sent to Datong Hospital for treatment. However, his injuries are very serious, and his life may be in danger.

Liyang 91

The Tragic Situation of the Liyang Floods: This time, the continuous rain caused a disaster, and the mountain water burst out. The water in Liyang County was several feet high, and the villages and fields were all submerged. The residents were trapped by the water and had no way to escape. Those who climbed trees and roofs, stretching their necks and looking for help, were everywhere. The rest either slept in the open on high ground or begged for food in the city. It is not known how many more there are. According to various investigations, the area is more than forty miles long and sixty to seventy miles wide. There is not a single field that has not been submerged, and not a single seedling can be seen. There are nearly 100,000 disaster victims waiting for relief. The local area has suffered from various disasters, including soldiers and bandits, and the economy is in a desperate situation. There is no way to provide assistance. It is said that the local gentry Di Xinzhi, Di Jianren, Zhou Qingsheng, etc. have been publicly elected by the Flood Relief Association to go to Shanghai to beg for relief from the Jiangsu Flood Relief Association and various charitable organizations and philanthropists.

Nantong 92

The Dispute over Converting Cash into Silver Dollars is Not Yet Resolved: Nantong's public education funds are deposited in money shops and pawnshops to generate interest. Because the deposit was calculated in cash, disputes have arisen over the conversion into silver dollars over the years, and they have not yet been resolved. Currently, money merchants Liu Zhongze et al. have filed a request with the court for legal mediation.

The Yan Zheming Case is Difficult to Proceed: The 18th Team of the Provincial Water Public Security stationed in Tong shot and killed Yan Zheming in front of the court. The prosecutor's office has begun investigating and has summoned the shooters. Because this case requires an autopsy, it has sent a letter to the team headquarters pointing out the location of the buried coffin. The reply stated that the coffin had been taken away by Yan Qingshan, the brother of the deceased. Captain Xie has not yet returned to Tong. The case is proving very difficult to proceed, and it has been submitted to the High Court for review. The Notorious Bandit in the Northern Township is Captured: Xu Yuan, a notorious bandit in the northern township of Tongyi, specializes in kidnapping women, raping them, and selling them. He also gathers crowds to rob. On the twenty-first, he was captured by the police corps in Xiting and escorted to the county government for interrogation.

Zhenjiang 93

Representatives of the County Disaster Relief Association Go to the Department of Civil Affairs to Request Urgent Relief: The Zhenjiang County Party Headquarters and the County Government believe that the disaster situation in the county is serious and that there is an urgent need for rescue. Therefore, yesterday, they convened representatives of various agencies and organizations in the County Party Auditorium to hold a disaster relief meeting and elected seven agencies and organizations, including the Zhenjiang County Party Headquarters, as members of the Disaster Relief Association. After the meeting, Tan Peiyan of the County Party Headquarters, Zhang Peng of the County Government, Wu Shengfu of the Money Trade Association, Huo Rentai of the County Farmers' Association, and Zhao Xianbai of the County Chamber of Commerce jointly went to the Department of Civil Affairs to petition. Director Hu personally met with them and promised to do his best to allocate funds according to the opinions of the representatives.

The Unscrupulous Merchant Zhu Yuehua is Sent to the Public Security Bureau: The inspection team of the Provincial Public's Anti-Japanese Aid to Overseas Chinese Association discovered sixty bags of Japanese sugar being transported by Yao Yiwan's Fuxiang Company at the riverside the other day. They immediately ordered them to go to the Anti-Japanese Association to complete the registration procedures for Japanese goods before selling them. However, Zhu Yuehua, the manager of the company, refused to comply and acted unreasonably. Therefore, the Aid to Overseas Chinese Association sent a letter to the Fourth Branch of the Provincial Public Security Bureau, requesting that the manager be taken to the General Bureau for detention pending handling.

Yangzhou 94

The Tenth District's Disaster Situation After the Water Subsides: Although the water level in the Grand Canal has now stabilized slightly, there are still many dangerous sections along the canal. The Jiangdu section has purchased a large number of wooden piles and hired the Yuan Wheel to transport them to the construction site on the twenty-second for use. In the tenth district, the area from Hanjia Ditch, Baijia Lane, and Xujia Lane in the east to Huaizibiqao in the south and Huangbing Bridge in the north to Miaotou Town in Huohao Township is a sea of water. More than 70,000 disaster victims are mostly living by stealing lives from treetops. In the fourth district, the collapse of the Bihu Dam caused flooding of residential buildings, and the northwest corner has become a waterland.

The Jiang-Zhejiang Masses Gathered at the Shahe Dam: At about 9:00 AM on the twenty-first, nearly a thousand people from Jiang-Zhejiang gathered at Shahe Dam outside Dongguan, claiming to protect the dam. The county government telephoned the Jiangdu section for inquiries. The section stated that there was no talk of opening the dam and sent personnel to the dam to explain to the people. After a while, Zang Liuqi, the chief of the second district, also arrived by car and announced to the people that it was a rumor. However, the people were still unable to believe it and have sent representatives to the county to petition. The county government again told them that it was currently raising the height of the dam and that there was no talk of opening the dam. The people from Jiang-Zhejiang who came to protect the dam are still stationed at the dam and have not returned.

Ningbo 95

Rice Merchants Attempt to Manipulate Prices and Are Discovered: Due to the extraordinarily severe floods in various provinces, rice prices in Ningbo ports and rice shops suddenly rose. Therefore, unscrupulous merchants are doing a lot of speculative business by selling short. The rice merchant in charge of this matter is Shunhe Rice Shop on Houtang Street, Jiangdong. The shop was opened by Shi Jitang. Shi believes that Ningbo's rice prices are based on Shanghai prices. Therefore, he secretly sent Secretary Zhang Zhongying (also known as Amao) to Shanghai to counterfeit the seal of Dacheng Rice Shop in Shanghai. On the seventeenth, he telegraphed various large and small rice shops in Yongdi, reporting false price quotations. The rice shops in Ningbo received the telegram and registered with the telegraph office. However, the telegrams were all bookstore names, which was quite suspicious. Therefore, they telegraphed Dacheng to ask about the actual rice prices and asked if they had sent a telegram. They received a reply stating that they did not admit to any of this. They then realized that someone was forging telegrams in order to manipulate prices and profit. Therefore, the managers of each shop discussed with each other and secretly plotted to find a remedy. At 11:00 PM that night, Xu Guo ran into two salesmen, Shen Zirong and Zou Guangming, at the Xinxin Dance Hall. He promised to give them a reward of 500 yuan and asked them to find a way to crack the case. On the morning of the eighteenth, the two salesmen took eight policemen to wait at the port. They saw Amao coming down from the Ningxing ship in a hurry. They detained him, took him to the first branch of the second district, and found two receipts for the telegrams and a forged seal on the spot. It is said that Amao was temporarily bailed out by the Jiangdong Xiangtai Lumber Company. When the party and government agencies heard about this, they ordered the Rice Industry Association to investigate and verify the matter.

Feng Songqing is Kidnapped: Feng Zifan, a gentleman from Houchang, Yinxi, is the father of Feng Songqing, who owns a business and is somewhat well-off. At about 10:00 PM the other night, four bandits suddenly came with guns, broke down the door, and robbed a small alarm clock, a leather box, and two cheongsams, as well as more than ten silver dollars. After the looting, they kidnapped Feng Zi and took him out the door, heading south. When the detective team heard about it, they ordered each detective to investigate in different directions.

Letter to the Editor

Letter from Bao Xiangzhong of Yangzhou 96

Dear Editor, I was very surprised to read the news item "The Yangzhou Sub-Service Member's Scheme to Entice a Singer Case" in the Yangzhou Communications column of your newspaper on August 19. According to the report, the prostitute Hua Yuchun claimed on August 1 that she did not want to be a prostitute and entered the Women's Relief Center. Mother Shen Gu suspected that Zhao Zhentan was one of the customers and suspected him of enticing her. Because Zhao has a marital relationship with me, she further falsely accused me of colluding with him. You should know that I have not inquired about matters within the Relief Center since I resigned as director of the Relief Center in March. Moreover, when Shen Yuchun entered the Relief Center, I was in Jingkou receiving medical treatment due to illness. When I heard the news and returned, I learned that the woman had been instigated by others to make all kinds of slanders. I filed a lawsuit with the Jiangdu County Court, accusing her of pointing out facts, damaging the reputation of others, falsely accusing me, and intending to subject others to criminal and disciplinary actions. On August 18, the prosecutor's office opened a court to investigate the matter. After the interrogation, it ordered Shen Gu to pay a bail of 200 yuan and obtain a shop guarantee to await summons. As for the superintendent's dismissal of me and the dispatch of personnel to recover my credentials, this has not happened to this day. I am writing to request a correction. I would be most grateful. Sincerely, Bao Xiangzhong, August 22,

Education News

Important News

Implementation Plan for Establishing Secondary Agricultural and Industrial Schools in Provinces and Cities 97

The "Implementation Plan for Establishing Secondary Agricultural and Industrial Schools in Provinces and Cities" drafted by the Ministry of Education, along with the implementation plans for three types of specialized schools: agriculture, medicine, and engineering, were simultaneously approved by the 276th Central Political Conference. The Ministry of Education will soon issue a directive to all provinces and cities to comply. The text of the plan is recorded below:

(1) Secondary Agricultural Schools

(A) Establishment Methods: 1. Each province should first establish one secondary agricultural school in each former circuit district. Approximately four to five schools per province. If a province's finances are genuinely difficult, the schools may be established over three years. 2. After each province has established the required number of secondary agricultural schools in the former circuit districts, additional schools should be added to the former prefectural areas or the larger counties under the direct jurisdiction of the former subprefectures, one school per district, to be completed within three years. 3. Each district should select the village within the district that has the most wasteland and is easily accessible from all counties within the district as the location for establishing the secondary agricultural school. 4. Each secondary agricultural school must be attached to a farm of at least 500 mu and a forest farm of considerable area. If a forest is established, it should be attached to a forest farm of at least 1,000 mu. If it is not easy to allocate or purchase this amount of land at once, it may be gradually expanded, but it must meet the minimum requirement within three years at the latest. 5. Students entering the secondary agricultural school must have graduated from junior high school or have equivalent academic ability, be physically strong, and be willing to engage in agriculture after graduation.

(B) Establishment Standards: 1. The purpose of secondary agricultural schools is to cultivate talent capable of independently managing various agricultural activities, farm technicians, farm instructors, agricultural extension officers, personnel for farmer cooperation and rural improvement, and primary school agriculture teachers. 2. In addition to the compulsory general agricultural courses, secondary agricultural schools may offer courses in forestry, sericulture, etc., depending on local agricultural conditions and the financial resources of the province. 3. The duration of study in secondary agricultural schools is set at three years. 4. The proportion of time spent on classroom instruction and practical work in secondary agricultural schools should be approximately equal. 5. Secondary agricultural schools do not have summer vacations, but classwork may be reduced during hot weather. 6. Secondary agricultural schools should focus on agriculture, promote farmers' economies, rural improvement, and cooperative endeavors. 7. Secondary agricultural schools should be attached to agricultural cooperative organizations to facilitate practical training. 8. Secondary agricultural schools should be attached to a simple agricultural museum (including farm tools and agricultural products) and may hold agricultural exhibitions. 9. Secondary agricultural schools should be attached to an agricultural extension department to effectively connect with farmers around the school and implement agricultural improvement initiatives. 10. Secondary agricultural schools should be attached to farmers' supplementary schools and various short-term agricultural training courses, to be determined as needed depending on the environment. 11. The construction cost of secondary agricultural school buildings is approximately 50,000 yuan per school, and the equipment cost is 30,000 yuan. The purchase cost of attached farms and forest farms, if purchased, must be raised separately. 12. The recurring expenses of secondary agricultural schools, with all grades in each department complete and two classes per grade, are estimated at 40,000 yuan per year.

(2) Secondary Industrial Schools

(A) Establishment Methods: 1. Any city with a population of 100,000 or more must establish one secondary industrial school. If there are multiple such cities in a province, the schools may be established sequentially over three years. 2. In addition to establishing one industrial specialized school in each city under the direct jurisdiction of the Executive Yuan, one secondary industrial school must also be established, either attached to the industrial specialized school or established independently. 3. After all secondary industrial schools in each city have been established, the cities should gradually increase the number of schools as needed, depending on the development of each school. 4. Students entering the secondary industrial school must have graduated from junior high school or have equivalent academic ability, be physically strong, and be willing to engage in industry after graduation.

(B) Establishment Standards: 1. The purpose of secondary industrial schools is to cultivate technical personnel for various industries, individuals capable of independently managing small industries, and primary school industrial teachers. 2. Secondary industrial schools are divided into departments such as mechanical engineering, electrical engineering, civil engineering, architecture, applied chemistry, dyeing and weaving, and ceramics. The departments to be established should be determined based on the local industrial situation and social needs. A school may establish one or several departments. 3. The duration of study in secondary industrial schools is set at three years. 4. Secondary industrial schools should be attached to factories with complete and sufficient equipment for students' practical training. 5. The proportion of time spent on classroom instruction and practical work in secondary industrial schools should be approximately equal. 6. Secondary industrial schools should establish close ties with local factories. Factories should provide opportunities for secondary industrial school students to visit, study, or receive practical training. 7. Secondary industrial schools should establish industrial exhibition rooms for research purposes. 8. Secondary industrial schools should be attached to industrial product societies to promote and extend the manufacture of domestic goods. 9. Secondary industrial schools should be attached to various short-term industrial training classes and adult supplementary classes, etc. 10. The construction cost of secondary industrial school buildings is approximately 50,000 yuan per school. If multiple departments are established, the cost of factory equipment, establishment, and recurring expenses should be increased accordingly. The regulations for each department are as follows: Establishment costs (including factory equipment costs): Mechanical and Electrical Engineering Department: 120,000 yuan; Civil Engineering and Architecture Department: 50,000 yuan; Applied Chemistry Department: 100,000 yuan; Dyeing and Weaving Department: 100,000 yuan; Ceramics Department: 50,000 yuan. Recurring expenses (based on all grades established and two classes per grade): Mechanical and Electrical Engineering Department: 80,000 yuan; Civil Engineering and Architecture Department: 50,000 yuan; Applied Chemistry Department: 80,000 yuan; Dyeing and Weaving Department: 80,000 yuan; Ceramics Department: 40,000 yuan.

Provinces and Cities that Should Establish Three Types of Specialized Schools: Agriculture, Medicine, and Engineering 98

1. Specialized Agricultural Schools: Each of the twenty-three provinces, including Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Hubei, Hunan, Fujian, Guangdong, Guangxi, Guizhou, Yunnan, Sichuan, Xikang, Xinjiang, Ningxia, Gansu, Shaanxi, Shandong, Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, the Eastern Provinces Special District, Rehe, and Suiyuan, Qinghai, should establish one school.

2. Specialized Medical Schools: Each of the twenty-six provinces, including Jiangsu, Anhui, Hubei, Hunan, Fujian, Guangdong, Guangxi, Guizhou, Yunnan, Sichuan, Xikang, Xinjiang, Ningxia, Gansu, Shaanxi, Shanxi, Henan, Shandong, Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, the Eastern Provinces Special District, Rehe, Suiyuan, Chahar, Qinghai, as well as the six cities of Nanjing, Shanghai, Qingdao, Beiping, Hankou, and Tianjin, should establish one school.

3. Specialized Industrial Schools: Each of the four cities of Nanjing, Shanghai, Qingdao, and Beiping should establish one school.

Normal School Trainees Allowed to Take High School Normal Department Entrance Exams 99

According to a report from the Jilin Education Department to the Ministry of Education, in the past, due to a lack of primary school teachers, the department formulated brief regulations for normal school training institutes, ordering them to be established by various counties and attached to schools in various provinces to meet the immediate need. Graduates of the three-year training courses were recruited from graduates of higher primary schools, and their curriculum was roughly the same as that of junior high school, except that the English subject was removed and educational subjects were added. Some of these graduates wish to continue their studies. Recently, because the English subject has been included as an elective in the normal school curriculum standards, these students have petitioned to be allowed to take the high school normal department entrance exams to deepen their knowledge. Upon investigation, these students originally possess the same qualifications and years of study as junior high school students, except that they have not studied English, which is a special case. The matter concerns changing the entrance qualifications, and the department has wired to request an explanation of whether it is feasible. The Ministry of Education replied that if the normal school students in the province originally possess the same qualifications and years of study as junior high school students, they should be allowed to take the high school normal department entrance exams. You are hereby notified.

School Board Members Not Qualified to Serve as Educational Administrative Personnel 100

The Chahar Education Department inquired to the Ministry of Education whether the "xuetong" (school director) mentioned in Zhangbei County's previous report refers to the "xuetong" of public rural schools, some of whom are appointed by the county government or education bureau, and whether they are the same as the school board members of private schools, and whether they can be considered as having the qualifications of current educational administrative personnel listed in Article 16, Section 2 of the Education Association Law. The Ministry of Education replied that school board members of public and private schools at all levels shall not be regarded as current educational administrative personnel. You are hereby notified.
