Fifth District People's Amateur Sports Meeting of Jiangsu Province, Yesterday's Symposium 111

The Jiangsu Province Fifth District People's Amateur Sports Meeting held a symposium at the Shanghai County Education Bureau yesterday. Attendees included Zhang Shoubai from Songjiang, Xiang Wei Xian from Jinshan, Song Jinrong from Fengxian, Song Shizuo from Nanhui, Mao Zhiqian from Qingpu, Yang Zhixue from Chuansha, Yao Fusheng Shi She from Shanghai, and Chairman Shi She. The report items are omitted. Discussion items (1) How should the People's Amateur Sports Meeting in this district be started? As a result, due to the urgent time and insufficient preparation, and the difficulty in raising funds, this district sports meeting is planned to be temporarily cancelled. (2) How should the athletes participating in the meeting be produced? As a result, Songjiang was recommended to formulate the passing standards for each sport and send them to the meeting for distribution to each county for implementation. (3) How should the methods for this district to participate in the provincial meeting be specified? As a result, the following regulations are presented to the province for instructions: (1) The athletes in this district shall be selected by each county according to the passing standards set by this meeting. (2) Athletes from each county whose results do not meet the standards will not be selected. (3) Each county shall be limited to one athlete per sport. If two or more athletes exceed the standard, the better one shall be selected as the athlete. (4) The list of athletes from each county shall be sent to the district association (Shanghai) for reporting by September 10. (5) Songjiang is selected as the competition center for ball sports. The participating county teams shall report the location to the Education Bureau and forward it to the Songjiang County Education Bureau to compile the schedule. 4. How should the budget be specified? As a result, since the district sports meeting is not held, the expenses for participating in the provincial meeting shall be borne by each county. The province will subsidize 100 yuan, and the method of distribution will be determined after the meeting is over. 5. How should the national martial arts athletes be produced? As a result, each county shall select and send them on their own, limited to one athlete per county. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

China-Canada Forms Are Even 115

| Each Win One Singles |

Qiu Feihai (China) 6-2 6-1 6-0 Litt (Canada)

Qiu Feihai Immediately Overcomes The Enemy In the China-Canada match, Qiu Feihai and Litt were the first to bear the brunt. Canada seems to have used a trick by using Litt as the first singles, which should not have been done. With Qiu's skills, there is no question about winning against Litt. However, Qiu's performance yesterday was not the best. Perhaps because the enemy was weak, the wonderfulness was greatly reduced. Qiu served and won a game, and Litt also got a game, thus dividing the points equally at 2-2. Then Qiu won four consecutive games to win the first set. Litt only won the second game of the second set, and then the entire army was wiped out in the third set. Qiu didn't use much effort yesterday, and he often saw himself sacrificing the ball that he couldn't return, probably to save energy. Later, there were several very accurate corner shots, which were very spectacular. Litt has great arm strength. Qiu's racket once hit a serve, but he couldn't answer it. Unfortunately, double faults were piled up, and there were many suicides hitting the net. In the last set, he seemed to have no intention of fighting.

Jiang Daozhang Resist Defu Jiang De succeeded Qiu Li in the battle. Defu's profound skills were greatly displayed yesterday. Jiang had been cautious in the early stages of the war, intending to plot a resistance, and the war party knew that it was incomparable. There are many tricks in this group of hits, and the two often run up to block the net, while Defu's backhand volley on the net is smooth, powerful and beautiful. Jiang often had double faults and wild ball serves on the net, which often made the winning game fail. Defu's fast and urgent ball is especially noteworthy. In the first set, Jiang only won one game after one to five, and ended with two to six. In the second set, Jiang seemed to be invigorated, creating three to three numbers. Unfortunately, he lost three consecutive games again, and lost again at three to six. In the third set, after three to three, he lost two more games, and then recovered a game to lose at six to four. It is a pity that the two or three sets were relatively hopeful, but they did not succeed first. Jiang's skills have greatly improved compared to the past.

Local News

Zhu Qinglan Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday 119

To undertake disaster area relief work

Plans to inspect Wuhan soon

Zhu Qinglan, a standing committee member of the Disaster Relief Committee, arrived in Shanghai on the 20th by train from Tianjin in response to a telegram from Song Ziwen, the chairman of the National Government Relief Flood Committee, and Xu Shiying, the chairman of the Relief Committee, to handle flood relief affairs. Those who came with him included Cha Liangzhao, Anxin Tou Tuo, and Master Fan Cheng, all standing committee members of the North China Charity Federation. After getting off the train, Zhu immediately visited Finance Minister Song Ziwen and had a long and cordial conversation. The disaster relief methods were discussed in detail. Minister Song personally asked Zhu to take charge of the disaster area relief work, which Zhu had agreed to. He immediately telegraphed Pingjin, Jilin, and other places to invite many experienced relief workers to come to Shanghai, so that they could be distributed to various places to distribute emergency relief funds so that they would not be wasted and the disaster victims would receive more benefits. Last night, all sectors held a banquet for Zhu at the Jue Lin Vegetable Hall. Xu Shiying and Wu Zhihao, among others, were present and discussed flood relief on the spot. Yesterday, our newspaper reporter specially visited Zhu, who said that he had been in Shaanxi for relief and inspected the disaster situation in Gansu for more than two months. After arriving in Zhengzhou, he was summoned by Deputy Commander Zhang to handle emergency relief in the war zone, so he hurriedly returned to Ping from Zheng. After receiving the telegram from Shanghai, he packed his bags and went south. On the evening of the 18th, he arrived in Tianjin and participated in the founding meeting of the Tianjin Water Disaster Emergency Relief Association on the 19th. He left Tianjin for Shanghai on the 20th. Regarding the disaster relief methods, it was decided that he would discuss the methods in detail with Minister Song, etc. at the Disaster Relief Association tomorrow morning (that is, this morning) at nine o'clock. After staying in Shanghai for a short period of time, he also plans to personally go to the disaster areas such as Wuhan to inspect everything.

Disaster Relief Fundraising from All Walks of Life Yesterday's News 120

The floodwaters in the disaster area are gradually receding, and disaster relief efforts are underway

Looking at yesterday's news, the floodwaters in the disaster area seem to have gradually receded, and disaster relief efforts from all walks of life are underway. However, the salt shortage and the problems of accommodation and epidemic prevention are quite challenging for the relief workers to study. The various news heard yesterday is compiled as follows:

Important News Received Yesterday 121

Baker Telegraphed that the Han River is Gradually Receding: According to the Water Disaster Relief Committee, Mr. Baker telegraphed from Hankou on August 22nd, stating that aerial reconnaissance over the Han River basin revealed that the water was gradually receding. Most of the land had become mud, and the flooded area extended 60 miles northwest from Hankou.

Minister Song Ordered Merchants to Transport Salt to Aid the People: According to the National News Agency, yesterday's telegram from Hankou stated that the salt reserves there were entirely submerged, causing hardship for merchants and salt scarcity. The reporter specially called on Minister Song to inquire about the measures being taken. Minister Song replied that he had ordered the Hubei Salt Monopoly Bureau to supervise merchants in moving salt and had sent officials to survey the situation in order to salvage it. He had also ordered merchants to continuously transport salt by land and distribute it to various banks to supply the people with food. As for the concerns of Hubei banks and salt merchants that the current salt tax was high and the new salt law stipulated a lower salt tax, and that transporting and storing salt on various banks might result in losses when the new salt law was implemented, Minister Song stated that laws and regulations have implementation periods. Before the implementation of the new salt law, the government would definitely consider the situation and properly plan to ensure that salt merchants do not suffer any losses due to the reduction of the new salt tax. Merchants should not worry excessively.

The Social Bureau Drafted Measures for Sheltering Disaster Victims: This year's flood is massive, and it is reported that hundreds of thousands of refugees from affected provinces will come to Shanghai, making it urgent to find ways to accommodate them. The Social Bureau has already sent letters to various organizations, inviting them to a meeting tomorrow. It has also drafted a plan for sheltering the refugees, preparing a proposal for discussion and deciding on its implementation.

The Naval Department Dispatched Warships to the Han River for Disaster Relief: The Municipal Chamber of Commerce, deeply saddened by the suffering of the people in the Hankou flood, telegraphed the Navy Department to send warships to assist in rescuing the disaster victims. The Chamber received a reply from the Navy Department yesterday, which read: "To the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, your telegram has been received. All warships are currently engaged in suppressing bandits in various locations but will be dispatched to provide assistance as much as possible. Sincerely, the Navy Department, [day of the month]."

The Relief Committee Telegraphically Remitted Relief Funds to Three Provinces: The Shanghai office of the Relief Affairs Committee received three telegrams from the Beijing headquarters regarding urgent flood relief, as well as telegrams from the Shanghai office remitting large amounts of relief funds. The messages are recorded as follows: "To the Relief Committee's Shanghai Office, your telegram has been received. 20,000 yuan in epidemic prevention relief funds remitted from the Central Bank to Hankou has been received in full on [August] 21st. Please acknowledge receipt. Relief Affairs Committee, Yang [illegible], Committee Chairman: Your telegram has been received with respect. We have already taken the liberty of allocating 6,000 yuan to Committee Member Yan Zhuang (referring to Committee Member Yan Zhuang who is going to Anhui and Jiangxi for urgent relief). Committee Member Yan has agreed to depart tomorrow. [The rest is omitted.]" "[Three:] To Secretary Jin Guanfu, your telegram has been received. The relief funds for Henan Province were telegraphed to the Committee Chairman in Beijing yesterday. Sincerely." The Shanghai office also sent a telegram to the Relief Affairs Committee: "To Committee Members Yan Zhuang and Wang [illegible], Secretary Huang [illegible], Section Chiefs Hao and Zhou, Relief Affairs Committee, Nanjing Jiabao Gallery: 170,000 yuan for Anhui relief, 120,000 yuan for each of Henan and Jiangxi provinces, totaling 430,000 yuan, were remitted by the Central Bank for 200,000 yuan, the Bank of China for 100,000 yuan, and the Central and South Bank for 130,000 yuan. Please check and acknowledge receipt. Wang Zhen, Shanghai Office, respectfully."

Li Zushing Flew to Hankou Yesterday Morning: Relief Affairs Committee member Li Zushing, carrying 170,000 yuan in donations for the flood and 55,000 yuan in donations jointly raised by the Ningbo Association, Siming Guild Hall, and Shaoxing Yongxintang, flew from Shanghai to Hankou at 8:00 AM yesterday morning to distribute the funds in the disaster area.

Ningbo Community Held a Meeting to Urgently Aid the Hankou Disaster: The Ningbo Shanghai Association and the Shanghai Siming Guild Hall convened a general meeting yesterday at the Association's lecture hall on Tibet Road to discuss ways to urgently aid fellow Ningbo natives affected by the disaster in Hankou. Over a hundred people attended, and Yu Qiaqing was elected chairman. The chairman declared the meeting open, briefly stating that the disaster in Hankou was extremely severe, and fellow Ningbo natives in Hankou were suffering in dire straits. The Association, along with the Shaoxing seven counties Shanghai Association and the Shanghai Siming Guild Hall, had organized an emergency relief team to Hankou, carrying food and medicine, but urgently needed funds. He requested all fellow Ningbo natives to actively donate and contribute to the righteous cause. Zhang Shenzhi then reported on the situation of the emergency relief efforts in Hankou. The meeting then discussed fundraising methods. Mr. Wu Zhihao proposed dividing the fundraising into two categories: assigned fundraising and donations. Those assigned to fundraise would be responsible for a team, with a quota of 2,000 yuan, while those making donations would freely sign up for the amount they wished to donate. The goal was initially set at 200,000 yuan. Mr. Fang Jiaobo seconded the proposal, and it was passed after discussion by the chairman. Those who signed up for assigned fundraising on the spot included Wu Yaqin, Mao Heyuan, Lou Xunru, Yuan Ludeng, Zhang Jiguang, Chen Songyuan, Fang Jiaobo, He Shaoting, Wang Guanxin, Sun Meitang, Xu Shengchan, Wang Boyuan, Yu Zuoting, Hong Xianfang, Fang Shiru, Ge Yuchen, Yang Yongxiang, Wu Zhihao, Zheng Chengqing, Li Zhexiong, Zheng Yuanxing, the Zhejiang Ningbo Guild Hall, Zhang Shenzhi and Cai Qinshun (jointly), Zhu Meixian and Jin Runxiang (jointly), Feng Jingzhai and Shi Zhikun (jointly), Ge Yuchen and Zhu Zikui (jointly), totaling twenty-six teams (52,000 yuan). Donors included Zhang Yongni (2,000 yuan), Xin Yunqing (1,000 yuan), Dong Xingsheng (1,000 yuan), Qin Runqing (500 yuan), Lu Weirong (500 yuan), as well as Chen Chuxiang and Chen Zhonggao (200 yuan each), totaling 20,000 yuan. The total of the two categories was 72,000 yuan. Fellow Ningbo natives who were unable to attend the meeting due to other commitments would also be solicited for donations separately.

Jiang Zuobin Formed a Shanghai-Based Relief Fundraising Office: The Hubei Flood Emergency Relief Association held its tenth executive committee meeting on the 21st and resolved to send a telegram to twelve fellow Hubei natives in Shanghai, including Jiang Zuobin, to organize a Shanghai-based relief fundraising office. They also mailed thirty donation booklets on the same day. After receiving the telegram, Jiang and the others temporarily set up an office at No. 78 Gongshun Lane, Wuma Road, and scheduled an inaugural meeting for tomorrow to elect responsible personnel and raise relief funds to save the people affected by the disaster.

Continued Report on the Hubei Association's Fundraising Efforts: The Hubei Shanghai Association's Hubei Province Flood Emergency Relief Committee issued a fundraising appeal yesterday, stating: "Our Hubei is unfortunately struck by a heavenly disaster. Since the beginning of summer, incessant rain has led to mountain torrents, like water pouring down from a high roof. The Yangtze and Han rivers have overflowed, like arrows shooting through rapids. The levees have been breached, and houses have been washed away. Plants are swept along by the waves, and corpses float down the river. The plains have turned into a swamp, boundless and limitless. The highlands appear like floating bubbles, disappearing in an instant. The submersion of the city of Jinyang is not enough to compare to its extent, and the flooding of the seven armies cannot be compared to its magnitude. Moreover, the disaster area has reached over forty counties, and the number of disaster victims exceeds several million. Speakers are silenced, and listeners shed tears. It is truly a unprecedented catastrophe. We, as fellow natives, are concerned about our homeland and pity the displaced. We see bodies that have not yet turned to worms, suffering the misery of swimming with fish and turtles. The young and strong cry out in hunger on the road, while the old and weak wail on the mountain peaks. The urgency is greater than fire burning eyebrows, and the danger is akin to total destruction. If we borrow the ferry of compassion, we must spread the gold of the earth. When the滔天 is subsided and the安澜 is celebrated, when we find the millet and sorghum in the ruins of the graves and tread on the mud and sand of the flat ground, there is no hope of a harvest in the autumn, and how can we plan for clothing and food in the winter? It is unbearable to think of not providing relief early. Therefore, we have organized the Hubei Province Flood Emergency Relief Committee under this association to solicit donations and relieve the disaster victims. However, a cup of water is useless to a cart of burning firewood, but those with hair tied in crowns and those with disheveled hair all have compassion. We hope that those who uphold morality and benevolence and those who are compassionate will not shirk their responsibility, but will be courageous and act righteously. Either share Bao Shu's gold or contribute Chun Ren's wheat. The more the better, every grain is a pearl, reducing the flow of springs in the four seas and widely reviving the lean in the ditches. Pour down the sweet dew of the nine heavens to revive the souls at the bottom of the cauldron. We sincerely hope for your kind understanding." Yesterday, we also received a notification from the Shanghai Bank, stating that donations received included: Shanghai Kangcheng Winery (500 yuan), Guan Huai Shantang (250 yuan), Zhou Zhizang and Zhou Miaohai Lay Buddhist (200 yuan each), Chen Jingshan and Fang Keji (200 yuan each), Yu Jiyitang (150 yuan), Tongyi, Zhou Shengchao Lay Buddhist, Wu Shan, Song Jijiucui, Zhengda, Yuchun, and Xia Kunshan (100 yuan each), Tongfeng, Guan Zhuangzhu, Guan Jingzhi, Song Jiju, Guan Yingui, Dafeng, and Yuqing (50 yuan each), She Angxiao (40 yuan), Liang Wanfa, Kedai, and Chongyu (30 yuan each), Yan Xintai, Hengxingxiang, Zhenji, Dunhoutang, and Hongyu (25 yuan each), Peng Zhongshan, Hu Hengfeng, He Xinshun, and anonymous (20 yuan each), Hu Hongcheng (15 yuan), Xiong Jingcheng (12 yuan), Juyuanxiang, Zhou Fuji, Guan Chuhui, Tingsongji, Mingji, and Zhang Cengzhan (10 yuan each), Yu Yuantai, Tianfaxiang, Wei Yongshun, and Jinyushu (5 yuan each), Zhang Runshi (4 yuan), Yan Jinting (3 yuan), Shunhan (2 yuan), Hu Laojiu (1 yuan), totaling 3,302 yuan.

The Japanese Consul's Response is Absurd

Regarding the case of Japanese soldiers looting and assaulting inspectors of Japanese goods from the Anti-Japanese Aid Overseas Chinese Association, after the municipal government sent a letter to the Japanese Consulate General on the 14th of this month to lodge a serious protest, the Japanese side considered the matter until yesterday morning, when they sent a formal reply. The content did not fully address the three demands for guarantees of compensation and punishment of the perpetrators. However, it is reported that the Japanese side claimed that the soldiers' actions were legitimate acts of rescuing merchants, which is absurd. After the municipal government received the Japanese side's reply, Mr. Murai, the Consul General of the Japanese Consulate, visited Mayor Zhang at the municipal government but left without achieving any results. It is still unknown whether the municipal government will lodge another protest against the Japanese side's reply and what its attitude towards the reply will be.

Chamber of Commerce Issues Circular to All Guilds to Expose Fellow Traders Selling Japanese Goods 127

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday issued a circular to all trade guilds in the city, stating: Respectfully, on the 21st of this month, we received a letter from the Japanese Goods Inspection Committee established by this Chamber, stating that a permanent economic severance with Japan requires the self-awareness of merchants to be effective. Many merchants in our business community understand the greater good and genuinely resist Japanese goods, but it is feared that there are those who are blinded by profit and disregard the overall situation. Once someone intends to deceive, it will be impossible to prevent it. One bad apple spoils the whole bunch. Urgent preventive measures should be taken to safeguard the honor of all our merchants. Trade guilds are the leaders of their respective industries, with a deep understanding of the business conditions and the integrity of their members. Prevention can be thorough, and exposure will be effortless. If each trade guild regularly monitors the operation of its industry regarding Japanese goods and is responsible for reporting violations, then even cunning merchants will be exposed and unable to succeed. The day when we thoroughly eliminate inferior goods and defeat Japanese imperialism will surely come. The Chamber, having seen this, resolved in its first executive committee meeting to request your esteemed guild to forward a letter to all trade guilds, responsible for reporting fellow traders selling Japanese goods on record. We hereby record this for your information and urge prompt implementation, expressing our deepest appreciation, etc. Upon examination by the Chamber, each trade guild is responsible for correcting and reporting the actions of its members. Moreover, economic severance with Japan concerns the survival of the nation, making the situation even more significant than the usual "correction of business malpractices." Since each guild is closely monitoring and easily investigating, if reports are made promptly, those who violate the agreement for personal gain will be deterred. If the truth is concealed, not only will the meaning of "merchant self-regulation" be completely lost, but it will also create unnecessary chaos and invite criticism from the outside world. We issue this particularly earnest notice, hoping for strict attention and diligent handling. The Chamber will observe the determination of each guild in handling this matter, etc.

British-Owned Buses to Halt Service Entirely Today 128

Company Prepares to Hire New Workers, Managed to Keep a Few Routes Running Yesterday

Following the strike by all ticket sellers of the British-owned China General Omnibus Company, Routes 1, 2, 5, and 9 managed to operate with difficulty yesterday. The terms of employment have not been negotiated. All routes will completely cease operation today. The company is preparing to hire new workers. The arrested workers have been released. The various situations yesterday are recorded below:

Negotiations Still Stalled After all ticket sellers went on strike on the 20th, the strike committee presented nine terms of employment. Five representatives were sent to the company for negotiations that day, but the traffic superintendent refused to accept them. The strike committee has not sent representatives for contact in the past two days, insisting on continuing the strike, making a resolution difficult for the time being.

Route Conditions Yesterday, ticket inspectors continued to act as ticket sellers on the buses. Ten buses operated on Route 1 from Jing'an Temple to the Park Shooting Range, six on Route 2 from Er Yang Jing Bridge to the Park Shooting Range, three on Route 5 from San Mao Ge Bridge to the North Station, ten on Route 9 from Jing'an Temple to the Power Plant, one A Express, and one C Express, totaling thirty-one buses. The operating hours were from 6:00 AM to 8:00 PM. The remaining Routes 3, 6, 7, and 10, etc., are still suspended due to a lack of ticket sellers.

Service Suspended Today The British-owned China General Omnibus Company issued a notice yesterday by Traffic Superintendent Mr. Byatt (transliteration), stating, "All staff will be granted a special holiday on the 23rd of this month. Normal service will resume on Monday. This notice." Due to this, Routes 1, 2, 5, and 9, which managed to operate with difficulty, will also be suspended today. The public buses in the Public Concession will cease operations entirely today. If the ticket seller strike is not resolved by tomorrow, the ticket inspectors will continue to act as ticket sellers, managing to operate a few routes.

New Workers Hired After holding a board meeting on the morning of the 20th, the company, in addition to finding ways to restore all routes of public buses, reportedly requested the General Inspectorate of the Municipal Council to recruit new ticket sellers. The General Inspectorate had already hired dozens of people yesterday and sent them to the company's main factory at 263 Connaught Road in the morning for training. Once the training is completed, they will be dispatched to work on various bus routes.

Authorities Taking Precautions Since the British-owned public bus ticket sellers went on strike, Ren Liping, the Sixth District Chief of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, has not only sent personnel for thorough investigation but has also dispatched long-term police officers to guard the vicinity of the main factory on Connaught Road for several days to prevent any disturbances. Because the area is an extraterritorial road built by the Municipal Council, the Gordon Road Police Station has also dispatched patrol officers to guard the area for prevention.

Workers Released Two new ticket sellers, numbers 45 and 240, who were arrested by the Gordon Road Police at the intersection of Connaught Road and Jiaozhou Road in western Shanghai on the morning of the 21st of this month, have reportedly been released after being questioned by the police chief.

Local News II

Russian Impersonates Official in Arms Trafficking Case 129

Debate Concluded Yesterday, Judgment Scheduled for the 29th

The Russian, Leviskei Peek, and the Chinese, Wei Xiaolan, colluded to impersonate officials of the National Government, ordering over 1.8 million yuan worth of arms from the British trading firm, Lai Far. They forged seals, altered documents, and attempted to extort money from Zhu Ziyao, the owner of the Qiu Xin Factory, through intimidation. The Public Security Bureau filed a public prosecution, and the First Special Court has repeatedly summoned them, scheduling a date for the start of the debate. The details have already been recorded in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Xu Jiashi, the presiding judge of the criminal division, continued the trial in Criminal Division One. He first questioned Peek, asking if he had anything to say. Peek replied in English, which was translated by interpreter Jiang Baoliang, saying, "I have much to say, but all important documents are with my attorney, P. M. (French). Today, Attorney P. M. is not appearing in court because I cannot afford to pay the legal fees, and the documents have not been returned. This situation seriously harms the ethics of lawyers. I have nothing else to say." The court then ordered:

To begin the debate, Attorney Ru Bao-yi, representing the Public Security Bureau, rose and argued, "The Public Security Bureau accuses Leviskei Peek of violating Article 165 of the Criminal Law, impersonating a public official of the Republic of China, Article 224 of the same law, altering documents, Article 370 of the same law, extortion through intimidation, and additionally accuses Leviskei Peek personally of violating Article 234 of the Criminal Law, forging seals. Wei Xiaolan is accused of violating Articles 165 and 370 of the Criminal Law. Before debating the defendants' crimes, I will

Raise two points for the court's attention that are unrelated to this case. Because the defendant's lawyer will inevitably mention them, I, as the attorney, will raise them first. (1) Is Lai Far a seller of arms? Assuming that Lai Far is indeed selling arms, is he violating the law or breaking British law? Because the Public Security Bureau did not prosecute, we will not discuss it for now. (2) Did Lai Far sell the arms to the Cantonese? From a high-minded perspective, one would say that Lai Far is not helping the National Government but assisting the Cantonese faction, which could lead to other international discussions. However, this is irrelevant to the case and can also be disregarded. Now, regarding the defendant's

Criminal facts, let's discuss whether Zhang Faying exists. If he exists, is he actually Zhang Faying himself? The Public Security Bureau believes that he does not exist or is an imposter. According to the testimony of accomplice Wei Xiaolan, the two defendants, Leviskei Peek and Wei Xiaolan, told him that he could not act as a military commander, only as a secretary. This point is naturally disproven. Let's further examine whether the two defendants, Leviskei Peek and Wei Xiaolan, were impersonating public officials. The defendants went to the plaintiff's place, claiming to be military advisors to the National Government, and the National Government does have such positions, so regardless of who they are, they are committing a crime. However, Wei Xiaolan's impersonation as Secretary to Military Commander Zhang Faying does not need much debate because he

has already confessed. Has each of the defendants been to Lai Far? It has been proven by Lai Far, Carlo, and others, so their impersonation of public officials is very clear. Regarding the alteration of documents, on the contract, before the word "witness," the word "guarantor" was added. The defendant submitted a contract with the word "guarantor." The plaintiff submitted a contract without the word "guarantor." The Public Security Bureau's expert witness has previously proven that the word "guarantor" on the defendant's contract was added later. After adding the word "guarantor," the responsibilities of the witnesses, Carlo and Zhu Ziyao, become very different. According to British law, witnesses only prove the signing of the contract and do not cover fraud or intimidation. American law is the same, and

Chinese law must be similar. The guarantor's responsibility is different. If the contract cannot be fulfilled, the guarantor is responsible for fulfilling it. Therefore, a witness cannot also be a guarantor. If a guarantor also acts as a witness, in the event of a dispute, the guarantor can simply claim in court as a witness that there was indeed fraud or intimidation when signing the contract. Then the contract will certainly not be valid, and the guarantor will not be liable. Therefore, British law is very strict, and a guarantor cannot also act as a witness. Moreover, the plaintiff is British, and the contract was made with British people. How could the plaintiff not know this? The plaintiff has also entered into contracts before, so it is evident that

the defendant altered the document without a doubt. Furthermore, regarding the forging of seals by the defendants, the owner and employee of the Mei Tai Printing Bureau have testified that Leviskei Peek went to the printing shop and had a seal made to match Lai Far's seal. Public Security Bureau detectives have also testified that Leviskei Peek used Lai Far's stationery to stamp the seal when he picked it up. Although the defendants absolutely deny it, the evidence is undeniable. The reason they committed these crimes was to achieve their

goal of extortion through intimidation. They believed that the plaintiff was selling arms, so they would find another way to extort money. Suppose A steals someone's property, and B robs him. A is guilty of theft, and B is guilty of robbery. One cannot say that A's stolen property does not make B's robbery a crime. Initially, the Public Security Bureau was very doubtful about this case. When Wei Xiaolan was detained, the case became clear. Furthermore, Attorney Shi Zhuoren testified that the defendant hired him to demand a commission from Zhu Ziyao.

At that time, Attorney Shi told Zhu, "You are the guarantor, so you should bear the responsibility, and it is best to resolve this matter of arms." Attorney Shi did not believe there was any intimidating language, but Zhu Ziyao considered it extremely intimidating. Therefore, the defendant committed the crime of extortion through intimidation. I request the court to severely punish Leviskei Peek according to the law. Wei Xiaolan also had

helping actions, so I request that he also be punished." Following this, Attorney Fan Gang, representing Wei Xiaolan, argued that Wei did not know the details beforehand and was unwilling to go afterward, leading to a quarrel. Therefore, he requested the court to declare him innocent. Following this, Attorney Qiu Fenling, representing Peek and Leviskei, defended the two defendants according to the law. The key points were: (1) Military advisors do not have specific duties, so they cannot be considered to be impersonating public officials. (2) Alteration of documents, etc., cannot be directly proven to have been done by the defendants, so it cannot be established. Therefore, he requested that they be declared innocent. Judge Xu Jiashi then announced the conclusion of the debate and scheduled the verdict for the morning of August 29.

Midnight Gunfire 130

Man Shot and Killed on the Avenue du Parc

Three Gunshot Wounds Found on His Body

On the Avenue du Parc, built by the Municipal Council in the extraterritorial area, a murder occurred the night before last. The deceased was a young man, approximately twenty-five or twenty-six years old, wearing a Western suit, white shirt, white gabardine pants, black silk socks, and black leather shoes. Next to the body was a brown Western-style jacket and a felt hat. There were three gunshot wounds on his body: one in the back of the head, with the bullet lodged inside; one in the temple, with the bullet having passed through; and one in the chest, with the bullet not found. His entire body was covered in blood, a gruesome sight. He had a tattoo on his arm that had been removed with chemicals, leaving a large scar. The body was discovered near Guanghua University on Avenue du Parc between Lincoln Road and Zhongshan Road, a rather remote area. It is said that residents nearby heard several gunshots at approximately 11:30 PM when the incident occurred. It was also said that the victim appeared to have been brought to the location by car and then murdered by his enemies. Upon receiving the news, the Public Security Bureau of the Sixth District immediately dispatched police officers to the scene to investigate and apprehend the murderer. The body was unidentified, so they ordered the twenty-eighth Bao, seventh Tu, and local bailiff to report to the District Court for an autopsy. Prosecutor Yang and Examiner Shen arrived at the scene to conduct the autopsy and ordered the charitable organization to collect the body while awaiting the arrest of the murderer.

Zhao Shixi Killed by Gunshot Wounds in Robbery 137

Zhao Shixi, a 51-year-old resident of Dongchijiabang, Hongzhen, north of Shanghai, was a small landowner. It was rumored that he had a lot of money, which attracted the attention of bandits. At 11:00 PM the night before last, three bandits broke into his house. One bandit pulled out a gun to threaten him, and then they searched for valuables, stealing 21 yuan in cash. Dissatisfied, they continued to force Zhao to reveal the location of his hidden silver. When Zhao refused to give in, the bandits opened fire, shooting Zhao in the abdomen and foot. The bandits then fled in panic. Zhao fell to the ground, bleeding profusely and barely breathing. His family reported the incident to the Fourth Precinct of the Fifth District, which ordered the arrest of the bandits. Zhao was sent to Hongkou Tongren Hospital for treatment, but the bullet in his abdomen could not be removed, and he lost too much blood. As a result, the treatment was ineffective, and he died at 4:00 AM the next day. Upon learning of the incident, the Fifth District Precinct, in addition to reporting to the Public Security Bureau to dispatch detectives to track down the murderers, ordered Ling Renjie, the local bailiff of the Twenty-third Bao, Fifteenth Tu, to report the incident to the District Court. Prosecutor Yang and Examiner Shen arrived at the scene, examined the body, and determined that Zhao Shixi had died from gunshot wounds to the abdomen. They ordered the family to collect the body and await the arrest of the murderers.

Woman Kidnapped by Bandits 138

Ding Jinbao Plans to Return to His Hometown with His Mother

Kidnapped by Bandits Before Being Able to Embark

Shi Guibao Suspected of Having a Grudge Against the Woman's Father

Suspected of Coveting the Woman

Ding Zhushan from Yancheng makes a living by pulling rickshaws. He has two sons and one daughter. The eldest son, Jind, is twenty-two years old and married. The second daughter, Jinbao, is seventeen years old, and the youngest son, Jinlong, is fifteen years old. They live at No. 16 Feixing Lane, Xinmin Road, Zhabei, and own seventy rickshaws, doing well in business. At around 2:00 AM yesterday, Ding's wife and children got up because Ding's wife planned to return to her hometown that day with her daughter to purchase farmland, preparing to board a ship to Yancheng, Jiangbei, at 5:00 AM. Suddenly, six bandits arrived. Three bandits jumped in through the window, and three waited outside by the car that had been prepared. Among them, one wore a white Zhongshan suit, one wore a white silk gown, and the rest wore short clothes. After the three bandits entered the room, they closed the front door and used guns to drive Ding and his wife into the right-side room. They then broke into Ding's eldest son's new room on the left, snatched Jinbao, locked the front door, and drove away in the car towards Taiyangmiao on Datong Road. The victim, Ding Zhushan, immediately went outside to report the incident to the Fourth District police officer, who reported it to the headquarters. The headquarters immediately ordered detectives to investigate, but they had disappeared. After the chief asked Ding about the details, Ding said that Shi Yulu's son, Guibao, who was in the same industry, had asked to borrow one hundred coppers from him last week. Ding refused because he was unwilling to lend it to him. Guibao was very angry at the time, saying, "I'll give you what you deserve," and left. Guibao is suspected of causing this incident. After verifying the confession, the chief immediately ordered the police to arrest Shi Guibao at Feixing Lane, but he had already fled. They took his father, Yulu, to the station for questioning. According to neighbors of the family, the kidnapped woman, Jinbao, is quite attractive, and Guibao has been coveting her for a long time. Hearing that Jinbao was returning to her hometown with her mother and was going to be promised to someone else, Shi Guibao feared being disappointed and resorted to this measure.

Remarkable Success of Shanghai-Taicang Company's Fire Extinguisher Trial 142

The Shanghai-Taicang Long-Distance Bus Company recently purchased several large and small fire extinguishers from the Aurora Foam Fire Extinguisher Distributor at 363 Zhejiang Road, Shanghai, to be installed at various stations in Liuhe, Luodian, Jiading, Shanghai, etc., for fire prevention. At around 9:00 AM yesterday, a trial was conducted on an open space west of the Shanghai station. A wooden shed was constructed, doused with kerosene, gasoline, and other fuels, and then set ablaze. As the fire raged, Yang Yimin, a staff member from the fire extinguisher distributor, carried a fire extinguisher and sprayed white foam. Within a minute, the fire was completely extinguished, to the amazement of the onlookers. Subsequently, a large lead basin filled with gasoline was ignited and extinguished in the same manner. The burned wood and the remaining gasoline in the basin were covered with a thick layer of white foam, isolating the fuel from the surrounding air, effectively smothering it like a blanket. Observers then watched as the staff members from the distributor assembled the equipment and prepared the chemical powders. There were two types of powders, slightly yellow and white. Each extinguisher used one can of each powder, the size of the can depending on the capacity of the extinguisher. The yellow powder was mixed with seven times its weight in water, stirred well, and placed around the inside of the extinguisher. The white powder was mixed with an equal weight of water and placed in a glass tube, which was inserted vertically into the yellow powder solution, kept separate. The upper end of the glass tube had multiple holes. After everything was assembled, the lid was closed. The extinguisher had a nozzle at the end. In case of fire, the extinguisher was inverted, and the white powder solution in the glass tube flowed out, mixing with the yellow powder solution, creating a twelve-fold expansion of white foam that could be sprayed onto the burning material to extinguish it immediately. According to the staff members from the distributor, this prepared foam can be stored for up to three years without losing its effectiveness. A 1-gallon "housewife" model costs 40 yuan, a "vehicle" model costs 45 yuan, a 2-gallon handheld model costs 50 yuan, a "vehicle" model is also 50 yuan, a 5-gallon fire department model costs 80 yuan, and a 22-gallon wheeled model costs 500 yuan. All prices include the chemical powders. Refills cost 5 yuan, 6 yuan, 12 yuan, or 50 yuan, depending on the size. The effectiveness surpasses that of imported products, and all raw materials are domestically sourced.

Without sanitary medicines for prevention, epidemics will quickly erupt and be difficult to control. Recognizing this, the Xie Xing Pharmaceutical Factory in Shanghai has donated one case of "Sheng Dan" pills, totaling 12,000 pills worth 600 yuan, to Mr. Xiang Songmao of the Flood Relief Association for distribution in the disaster areas. These pills are known for their effectiveness in eliminating filth and preventing epidemics. They are commonly carried by travelers during summer and autumn and are especially important as a preventative measure in disaster areas where accumulated filth can easily breed epidemics. It is reported that these pills have already been shipped to the disaster areas along with other relief supplies.

Standardization of Weights and Measures in Shanghai 146

Following the declaration of standardization of weights and measures in Shanghai on the 1st of this year, reporters from the News Agency visited Director Pan of the Social Affairs Bureau and Director Zhou of the Weights and Measures Testing Institute yesterday to inquire about the progress of implementation. The following is a summary of their conversations:

The Supply and Demand in the Market are Sufficiently Balanced: Currently, there are 67 registered shops and factories manufacturing weights and measures in the city, employing 370 workers with a total capital of 35,000 yuan. In the spring of this year, the Testing Institute repeatedly ordered the shops to rush the production of new instruments for the market. However, at the beginning of the reform, most shops were hesitant and took a wait-and-see attitude. On the government's side, the implementation of the new system in various provinces and cities followed procedures stipulated by the central government, which could not be delayed. Thus, the Weights and Measures Instrument Manufacturing Co., Ltd. was established as a joint public-private venture with the approval of the Ministry of Industry, starting with loans and orders for the products of various shops. After the establishment of the factory in early May, the shops began to actively produce new instruments and submit them to the Testing Institute for verification. According to statistics, the number of items accepted for verification each month was 6,805 in May, 27,990 in June, and 42,385 in July. As of August 20th, it has reached 32,629 items. The number has been increasing month by month, so the overall output in one month is sufficient to meet the needs of that month.

Adherence to New Instruments and Destruction of Old Instruments: Since July 11th, the Testing Institute, in accordance with the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau's published first-phase inspection program for industrial and commercial weights and measures, has been conducting inspections in conjunction with the Public Security Bureau's district offices. The inspection of approximately 2,000 shops in the Hunan district is expected to be completed by September 26th. The second phase of inspections will then be announced for either the Zhabei district or the Special District. According to the regulations of the Ministry, from the date of the announcement of standardization of weights and measures in a certain area, new instruments should be used, and old instruments that cannot be repaired should be destroyed according to law. However, as this is the initial stage of implementation, the Testing Institute, to facilitate preparation by merchants and residents, only requires shops that have not yet purchased new instruments to set a deadline for switching to new instruments and to make a firm commitment. As the deadlines set by these shops are either imminent or have already passed, they are now being ordered to adhere to the deadlines and use new instruments, subject to reinspection. Those who deliberately violate the rules will have their old instruments destroyed without further leniency. The Testing Institute has also recently stipulated that uninspected shops will be given a notice to

Page 20

uniformly install new instruments and await inspection. If the manufacturing shops and factories are temporarily unable to supply enough new instruments, a purchase order should be obtained as proof, and it is not permissible to simply submit a commitment at the time.

Industries Conforming to New Instruments in Succession: At present, there are quite a few new instruments circulating in the market. According to reports from weights and measures manufacturing factories, in addition to the nearly 10,000 new scales purchased by vegetable stalls in the north and south markets, the number of new instruments purchased by various trade associations exceeding 200 is as follows: 1,200 items for the sauce industry, 700 items for the soy sauce and wine industry, 1,300 items for the dried goods industry, 390 items for the fruit industry, 350 items for the medicinal materials industry, 390 items for the cooked food industry, 261 items for the tea industry, 340 items for the candle industry, 206 items for the sugar industry, 200 items for the electrical machinery and silk weaving industry (above are weighing instruments), 500 items for the silk and satin industry, 500 items for the footwear industry, 1,000 items for the cotton cloth industry, 400 items for the embroidery industry, and 1,000 items for the ready-made clothing industry (above are measuring instruments). The scattered quantities purchased by other individuals or groups and those purchased directly from other shops and factories are not included, and the total number is estimated to have reached more than 50,000 items.

Inspection of the Concessions will Begin Soon: Regarding the inspection matters within the Public Concession and the French Concession, the French Concession had already reached an agreement with the Public Works Department in early July through Director Wei Zhiren, and the joint inspection matters were generally handled in accordance with the regulations stipulated by the Ministry. The French Concession also requested and obtained approval from the French Minister to implement the regulations in September. As for the Public Concession, Director Pan of the Social Affairs Bureau invited representatives from the Public Works Department for multiple discussions, and the Chairman of the Public Works Department, Mr. Macnaghten, met with Mayor Zhang to express his agreement to assist. Finally, Director Pan, based on the results of this meeting, and Chief Administrator Fei Xindun and Chief Patrol Mao Ding of the Public Works Department negotiated and finalized the assistance measures for the concession on July 7th. The main points are that the inspection matters within the Public Concession should be handled by inspectors sent by the Testing Institute with the assistance of the police, in accordance with the regulations stipulated by the Ministry. Penalties for violations of the law will also be jointly enforced by the Testing Institute and the assisting agency in accordance with the Weights and Measures Law. All procedures for transfer to the court will be handled in accordance with the usual procedures of the concession. However, in order to facilitate communication with the police, the Testing Institute should designate five or six inspectors, who must first meet with the police before starting their work. According to Chief Administrator Fei, the above measures will be implemented after being approved by the board of directors of the Public Works Department. However, due to the summer vacation, the board meetings were suspended, which delayed the process. It is expected that the measures will be approved and implemented after being submitted to the board in early September. Currently, factories in the city are preparing reserves of new instruments to meet the needs within the concessions.

Customs Must Also Implement the New System: This reform to the new system is a national policy and should be uniformly observed. The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau previously received a report from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, which in turn received a report from the Preserved Meat Industry Association, stating that the Shanghai Customs had not yet adopted the new system. The Bureau reported this to the Ministry of Industry, which then forwarded it to the Ministry of Finance, ordering the Customs to implement the reform so as not to hinder the implementation of the new system in Shanghai. Subsequently, a report in the Mainland News stated that, according to the Jianghai Customs authorities, although there had been rumors about the reform to the new system, it had not been officially reported in newspapers and had not been officially informed of the matter. This was quite surprising. The Weights and Measures Law was promulgated by the National Government, and as a government agency, how could it not be aware of it? This news was likely based on inaccurate reporting or on personal opinions of those who were not yet informed of the matter. Although it was a private conversation, its publication in the newspaper was sufficient to confuse the public. The Social Affairs Bureau then submitted a clipping of this news to the Ministry for instructions. Fortunately, the Ministry of Industry has instructed that it has forwarded the situation to the Ministry of Finance, ordering the Jianghai Customs to adopt the new system by a deadline, so the implementation of the reform is expected to be near.

Municipal Government Continues to Exempt Poor Households from Housing Tax 149

The Municipal Finance Bureau Issues a Notice

The Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau issued a notice yesterday, stating: Notice is hereby given that the Bureau collects housing tax for those whose monthly rent is less than one yuan and whose quarterly tax is less than three jiao, as they are mostly poor laborers who struggle to support themselves. A notice has already been issued exempting this portion of the rent from taxation. In order to show extra consideration, the Municipal Government has approved that from this autumn season, residents whose monthly rent is less than three yuan and whose quarterly tax is less than nine jiao will be exempted from paying the tenant portion of the housing tax. The landlord portion and the store housing tax are not exempted. Regarding the outstanding taxes from previous quarters, they are still required to be paid in accordance with the regulations in order to complete the accounts. In addition to ordering the collection offices to send staff to collect the outstanding debts, this notice is hereby issued for public information.

Anti-Opium Society Convenes a National Congress 150

Circular Has Been Issued

The National Congress of the Chinese National Anti-Opium Society, held every two years, is scheduled to take place from November 1st to 5th this year at West Lake in Hangzhou. The Society, recognizing the urgency of the date, should promptly inform local anti-opium organizations to prepare early and to formulate and nominate representatives and other procedures in order to comply. This circular was issued yesterday, and the original text of the notice is copied below. This Society convenes a general meeting every two years in accordance with its charter. This year marks the scheduled meeting, and it also coincides with the loosening of opium prohibition in the country, with divergent prohibition orders. Currently, public opium sales have been canceled due to enthusiastic opposition from comrades in various regions, but those advocating public sales are still operating in the dark, devising various plans and conspiracies to resurface. All anti-opium comrades should expand their campaigns and strengthen their organizations to prevent a relapse and to avoid the failure of years of anti-opium efforts in one fell swoop. Therefore, convening a national congress to bring together comrades from various provinces to encourage each other and to determine the grand plan of action is truly an urgent task for saving the times. Therefore, the Standing Committee of this Society resolved at its August meeting to convene the congress at West Lake in Hangzhou from November 1st to 5th. In view of the vastness of the national scope and the dispersed locations of the groups, it is necessary to appoint specialists to prepare in different regions in order to achieve twice the results with half the effort. The plan is organized as follows: (1) Meeting location: Xihu Grand Hall and Zhejiang Provincial Party Headquarters Grand Hall, West Lake, Hangzhou; (2) Meeting dates: November 1st to 5th; (3) Representative qualifications: Local National Anti-Opium Societies, Anti-Opium Propaganda Societies, and anti-opium organizations with similar characteristics to this Society, as well as individual members of this Society's joint organizations, may send representatives to attend. In areas where anti-opium organizations have not been established, representatives may be nominated by the Party Headquarters and civil organizations to attend as observers. In addition, Christian churches, Catholic churches, Buddhist associations, Muslim associations, and Confucian associations may also send representatives to participate. The selection methods and the number of representatives will be determined in detail separately; (4) Representative fees: Except for individual member representatives who will be provided by this Society when necessary, the travel expenses of representatives from various organizations will be borne by the respective organizations. However, this Society will, to the extent possible, write to the authorities to request a reduction in the train fares and other expenses for the representatives. Accommodation and meals in Shanghai and Hangzhou will be borne by this Society; (5) Regional preparation: For the convenience of communication, the country is divided into North China, Northeast China, South China, Southwest China, West China, East China, and Southeast Asia preparation offices. The North China Preparation Office is located at the Tianjin Hebei National Anti-Opium Society and includes the provinces of Hebei, Shandong, Henan, Shanxi, Chahar, Shaanxi, and Gansu. The Northeast China Preparation Office is located at the Shenyang Liaoning National Anti-Opium Society and includes the provinces of Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Rehe. The South China Preparation Office is located at the Fuzhou Fujian National Anti-Opium Society and includes Fujian, Guangdong, and Taiwan. The West China Preparation Office is located at the Chengdu Sichuan National Anti-Opium Society and includes Sichuan and Guizhou. The Southwest China Preparation Office is located at the Kunming Yunnan National Anti-Opium Society and includes Yunnan, Guangxi, and French Annam. The Southeast Asia Preparation Office is located at the Singapore National Anti-Opium Society and includes the British Straits Settlements, the Malay Peninsula, and the Dutch East Indies. The East China Preparation Office is located at the Hangzhou Zhejiang National Anti-Opium Society and includes Zhejiang, Jiangsu, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hunan, and Hubei. The National Preparation Office is located at the Shanghai Chinese National Anti-Opium Society; (6) Representative nomination: Local anti-opium organizations should convene meetings as soon as possible after receiving this notice, nominate representatives in accordance with the law, and register with their respective regional preparation offices to obtain qualification certificates and discounted train and boat tickets to prepare for departure; (7) Representative proposals: Local anti-opium organizations should prepare their proposals in advance and send them to this Society in Shanghai before October 15th for inclusion in the agenda, mimeographing, and distribution for discussion at the congress; (8) Congress promotion: This congress is of great importance to the future of the anti-opium movement of the masses. Local anti-opium organizations should make full preparations and carry out necessary promotion during the Anti-Opium Week in October, soliciting opinions from all sectors and submitting concrete articles to the congress; (9) Congress expenses: The expenses for convening this congress are enormous. Local organizations should donate according to their capabilities to show cooperation and strengthen their strength.

Annual Meeting of the National Medicine Trade Association 152

The National Medicine Trade Association held its annual meeting for the 20th year yesterday. More than 230 members attended. Zhang Meian, Zhuang Meitang, and Cen Zhiliang were elected as the presidium. After the formalities, the secretariat and finance department reported on the work of the association over the past year, as well as a summary of income and expenditure. Subsequently, the agenda was discussed, and the following resolutions were passed: (1) Regarding the new metric system, the industry believes it cannot be implemented due to its special circumstances and requests government assistance. It was resolved that the dosage of medicine is extremely important for the treatment of patients. If the new system is improperly implemented, it will inevitably affect the lives of patients. The government should be requested to exempt it from change according to the common practice of special medicinal dosages in various countries around the world in order to emphasize hygiene. (2) Regarding the new regulations of the French Concession Public Works Bureau on licensing pharmacies and the method of collecting business tax within the concession, and how the association should express its attitude, it was resolved that these regulations infringe upon the national sovereignty of hygiene administration, and the additional business tax is particularly damaging to the national tax law. The association should resolutely oppose it and proceed in unison with the New Medicine Industry Association. (3) Regarding the Ministry of Industry's division of the pharmaceutical industry's internal shop assistants to organize a labor union, and the external shop assistants to join the association, and what the association's opinion on this method is, it was resolved that pharmaceutical shop assistants have absolutely no need to organize a labor union in accordance with the law and reason, and the association should continue to strive against it. (4) Regarding the frequent incidents of members of the Fresh Medicine Industry Association arbitrarily raising prices and suspending the delivery of fresh goods, and how the association should handle it, it was resolved that the association should periodically invite the persons in charge of the Fresh Medicine Industry Association to the meeting to properly conclude a contract to facilitate compliance and prevent abuses. (5) Regarding the association's entrusted revision of labor and capital treatment conditions, which has been pending for many years and has not yet been resolved, and how to proceed, after this case was raised, the atmosphere in the entire venue suddenly became tense, with more than 20 speakers expressing their deep sorrow. Later, the chairman adopted the opinions of the public and resolved to urge the party and government organs to promptly comply with the order for resolution. (6) Regarding how to raise and pay the annual operating expenses of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, it was resolved to add one month's monthly donation to facilitate payment. (7) Regarding the chaotic selling prices among the industry, a price evaluation committee should be quickly formed to properly discuss methods to suppress the selling prices and benefit the sick. It was resolved that the general assembly publicly elect Cen Qisheng, Zhuang Meitang, Zhou Gansheng, Feng Jinpu, Zheng Baosheng, Chen Quanheng, Zhang Hongzhao, Shao Shilu, Cen Binghuang, Ge Kejian, Ding Defu, Sun Wenan, Yu Dongsheng, Xu Jiusong, and Liu Peiqing, 15 people to form a price evaluation committee, and Cen Qisheng will convene a meeting. (8) Regarding the proposed formulation of industry regulations, it was resolved that the former industry regulations committee should be reconvened by the association to formulate them. (9) Regarding the issue of members who do not pay donations according to the number of employees and those who fail to pay overdue fees, it was resolved that those who are in arrears should pay within a limited time. Those who do not pay donations according to the number of employees will be investigated by personnel and supplemented in full. (10) Regarding the practice of some colleagues receiving prescriptions and delivering medicine, which, although said to be convenient for patients, actually damages the business of smaller colleagues, and a request for a relief method, it was resolved that the freedom of business should not be discussed for the time being. After the discussion, the meeting adjourned at 6 o'clock.

Chen Xinghe Dies from Serious Injuries 159

The Second Person Injured by the Cement and Wood Frame

On the 20th at 12 noon, the Xinrongji Construction Factory was building a house for the China Arts and Crafts Society on Aimuyu Road in the French Concession. Five workers were washing their faces and having lunch in the shade of the northeast corner when the five-story veranda's cement and wood frame collapsed, crushing the head of the bricklayer Guo Peilong, who died on the spot. Chen Xinghe, Xu Changhui, Xu Fazi, and Wang A'gen were also injured, with their heads crushed and their limbs broken. After the police learned about it, they sent the injured to Guangci Hospital for treatment. Guo's body was carried to the coroner's office for autopsy. The details have been recorded in the newspaper. It is now known that Chen Xinghe, who was also crushed in the head at the same time, died at 5 p.m. on the same day due to excessive injuries. The next day, the hospital notified the police station and carried the body to the coroner's office of the Tongren Fuyuan Branch. After finding no relatives, the police station reported to the Second Special District Court to appoint Prosecutor Ding Shikui to go to the office at 10 a.m. to verify the body with forensic doctor Wei Ligong and clerk Zhao Yifen. According to the statement of the patrolman, Mr. Ding instructed that the deceased Chen Xinghe had died from injuries sustained during his lifetime, and since his family was not present, the Tongren Fuyuan Church would prepare a coffin for burial.

A Careless Fire at Xiaoshadu Thatched Sheds 162

Suddenly, thick smoke filled the air and penetrated the roof. Because the thatched sheds were connected, they were easily burned. The fire quickly spread to the surrounding dwellings. The fire was extremely fierce. The area was remote and narrow, making it difficult to rescue. Fortunately, the police on duty directed the crowd to immediately demolish the sheds to isolate them, and the fire gradually went out. A total of ten thatched sheds were destroyed. When the fire was raging, the cries of the poor people, both big and small, were deafening. The fire owner, He Jitao, jumped into the dense smoke and dragged out a small child. The child's feet were slightly burned. Seeing that he had caused the disaster, he fled with his wife and child. When the police station in charge of the Sixth District sent police to investigate, they could not find the fire owner. It was then said that the fire started between Nos. 393 and 4, so Zhu Xiucheng, a native of Funing at No. 393, was detained and escorted to the Sixth District Police Station for interrogation.
